Dominion Representatives Gather on Downing Street to Discuss the Current International Situation with British Cabinet Members; Both National Defense and Economic Issues Are Involved

(London) The Prime Ministers of Australia, New Zealand, Southern Rhodesia and South Africa gathered at 10 Downing Street for an informal discussion of the current international situation with British Cabinet members, lasting two hours. This is the second meeting in a week. The British Cabinet members attending were Prime Minister MacDonald, Lord President of the Council Baldwin, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, Dominion Secretary Thomas, Foreign Secretary Simon, and Colonial Secretary Lister. Foreign Secretary Simon gave a detailed account of the changes in the situation in recent months and provided information on the points the Dominions wanted to know. It is reported that further meetings will be held this week. (Reuters, 7th)

(London) Overseas representatives, gathered in London to celebrate the 25th anniversary of King George V's accession to the throne, held a meeting with British Cabinet members the other day to discuss the European situation. From today, they will resume their meetings to discuss imperial defense and economic issues. According to press reports, at today's meeting, representatives of the various Dominions raised a number of questions regarding the Far East, which Foreign Secretary Simon answered one by one, to the satisfaction of all parties. It is noted that this meeting does not decide British international policy, but only provides explanations to the representatives of the various Dominions, so that the British government still has the freedom to decide international policy. At today's meeting, what the overseas Dominions are most concerned about is the issue of British-Japanese relations. There are currently two major issues in British-Japanese relations: one is the competition from Japanese cotton textiles, and the other is the threat of Japanese naval expansion. Will Britain continue to be friendly with Japan, regardless of these issues? This is what should be discussed at the meeting. It is reported that the results of the discussion are that the first issue can be resolved if the Dominions can cooperate with the mother country. The second issue is related to the United States. The British government has reportedly assured the Canadian representative that Britain will not resolve this issue alone without the participation of the United States. From the British government's recent attitude towards Japan's promulgation of the Petroleum Law, which hinders the business of foreign merchants, we know that Britain is treating Japan in good faith. (Havas, 7th)

Canada Restricts Imports of Japanese Goods; Japanese Foreign Ministry Considers Countermeasures

Germany Plans to Approach Britain and Strengthen the Guarantee of the Locarno Treaty; This Will Be the Main Goal of Its Future Diplomacy

(Berlin) The German Foreign Ministry is now trying to approach Britain and wants to strengthen the guarantee of the Locarno Treaty. German Head of State Hitler sent a telegram of congratulations on the occasion of King George V's accession jubilee, in which he praised Britain's aspiration for peace. This is noteworthy. It is generally believed that Germany's pro-British attitude is clearly due to the reaction to the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty, which makes Germany uneasy. The German Foreign Ministry seems to be asking Britain for a detailed explanation of the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty and declaring that maintaining the Locarno Treaty is the main goal of German diplomacy. However, because Italy is busy with its colonies and fears that it cannot fully fulfill its obligations under the Locarno Treaty, it is using this as a reason to demand an increase in the guarantee of the Locarno Treaty. In addition, the German Foreign Ministry will ask France and Italy for a detailed explanation of the Franco-Russian mutual assistance treaty. Furthermore, the German Parliament was originally scheduled to convene on May 9, but has now been postponed to May 15 due to the King's accession anniversary. At that time, Hitler will deliver an important speech explaining German foreign policy. Hitler is now discussing German foreign policy with the newly built Scharnhorst large postal ship, the Minister of Defense, Blomberg, the Minister of Economic Affairs, Schacht, the disarmament representative, Ribbentrop, the party representative, Hess, and the Minister of Propaganda, Goebbels. (Havas, 6th)

U.S. Navy Aircraft Perform Aerial Combat Over the Ocean; Naval Experts Are Now Conducting Precise Research to Know to What Extent It Will Be Important in the Future

(Washington) The Navy Department announced today that the future of U.S. Navy aircraft depends entirely on the success of the performance of 450 aircraft in the current Pacific exercise. It is reported that all radio transmissions on the 150 warships have been specially ordered to cease, so even the official circles in Washington do not know where the "enemy" fleet is. (Tokyo) In order to strengthen its diplomatic array, Foreign Minister Hirota is dividing ambassadors stationed in various countries into groups such as China, Europe, North America, and South America, and deciding to hold ambassadorial meetings and consul general meetings in their respective central locations. The beginning of this was the Consul General Meeting held in Shanghai. However, in order to deal with the recent complex new situation in Europe, it was decided to hold a full European Ambassador Conference in Paris in early June, and Foreign Minister Hirota has already instructed Ambassador to England Matsudaira, etc. Furthermore, at the Ambassador Conference, Ambassador to England Matsudaira will serve as chairman, and the declaration of German rearmament, the attitude of various countries towards the military armament declarations of Austria, Turkey, etc., and Japan's policies, the intentions of related countries such as England, France, and Italy regarding the convocation of a naval disarmament conference, the possibility of Germany and Russia participating in the conference, and other diplomatic affairs will be reviewed within three days. Then, the results will be brought back to Tokyo by Ambassador Matsudaira, who will depart from London in mid-June, report to Foreign Minister Hirota, and make important recommendations. The Economic Influence of Soviet Russia in Northern Manchuria Declines Sharply; The Result of the Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

Osaka: According to a telegram from Harbin received by the Osaka City Industrial Department, with the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway, the entire Soviet influence has begun to retreat. As for the Soviet economic organizations in Harbin, only the Trade Representative Office and the Far Eastern Bank Turg Star and a few other places remain. It is learned that the above-mentioned places are gradually closing down due to various circumstances. The reasons are roughly as follows:

(1) Petroleum companies simultaneously announced their abolition due to the enactment of the Petroleum Monopoly Law by "Manchukuo." (2) The Pito firm attached to the Trade Representative Office has been reorganized and is liquidating its remaining goods and closing its doors. The Food Export Department has also completed its reorganization and has recently been abolished.

(3) The Trade Representative Office is scheduled to decide whether to retain or abolish it in two or three months. If the "Man" Soviet trade relationship can still be developed, it may be possible to reactivate it with special trade preferences. However, according to the current situation, the Soviet Union has no new commodities to import. (4) The Turg Fruit is the Soviet exchange agency in Manchuria. There are still many people who remit money to their relatives and friends in their home country, or it may be able to continue to exist as necessary. (5) The Far Eastern Bank has reduced its scale since the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway. It is expected that it will be closed by September at the latest, after the railway bureau staff has completely withdrawn. (Jiji News Agency, 5th)

U.S. Currency Plan to Be Broadcast on the Radio Next Monday; The Gold-for-Silver Proposal Is Not Being Considered

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau announced today that the United States is not giving much consideration to the gold-for-silver proposal. This statement was made by the Secretary when he met with the press. He also said that the details of the U.S. monetary system plan will be broadcast to the country next Monday by radio. Morgenthau avoided answering direct questions about the government's silver policy, but said that China's gold-for-silver plan has not yet been decided and has not been considered by the United States. At the same time, the price of silver in New York remained unchanged at 73 cents per ounce. (Guomin News Agency, 6th)

Graduation Ceremony of the Red Army Officer School; Stalin Delivers an Important Speech; The Period of Technical Hunger Has Now Been Overcome; Continue to Advance Toward Industrialization and Collectivization

(Moscow) Graduates of the Red Army Officer School gathered at the Kremlin on the 4th of this month. Stalin delivered a speech on the spot as follows:

"The legacy we inherited from the past was a technically backward, dilapidated, and impoverished country. Our country has experienced four years of the imperialist war and three years of civil war, so it has been almost completely destroyed. At that time, most of our people were illiterate, the level of technology was extremely low, and a few industries were like small islands in the ocean of agricultural farms. This is the legacy we inherited.

"Our task was to lead our country out of the track of the Middle Ages and ignorance and onto the track of modern industry and mechanized agriculture. This task was both heavy and difficult. The question at the time was as follows: Will we solve this problem in the shortest possible time and strengthen our country's socialism, or will we not solve this problem? In that case, our country will maintain its weak culture and ignorant culture, and will lose its independence and turn into a sacrifice of the imperialist powers. "At that time, our country went through a period of extreme lack of technology. Industry lacked machinery, and agriculture and transportation lacked machinery. At that time, we had no basic technical base, so there was no talk of industrialization. But we were finally able to move towards industrialization and collectivization with firm belief and enthusiasm. Today, this stage can be said to have been completed. Today, anyone can admit that we have made great achievements on this road. Today, anyone can admit that we have a strong and superior industrial organization, strong and mechanized agriculture, increasingly developed means of transportation, and a well-organized and well-equipped Red Army. All of this can show that we have largely overcome the period of technical hunger. "Although the period of technical hunger has passed, we have entered a new period in which all technical personnel should make further use of technology. Today, we have factories, collective and state-owned farms, and armies. We have all the technology, but our people do not have enough experience to make full use of this technology. Previously, we always said, "Technology determines everything." Today, our attention should be focused on the talents who can master technology. Therefore, the slogan "Technology determines everything" can only reflect the past period of technical hunger. As for today, it should be replaced by the slogan "Technical cadres determine everything." This is our main idea today. This slogan requires our country's leaders to give the greatest care and consideration to workers of all sizes in all aspects, to educate them, to assist them, to care for them, to encourage them if they have any requests, to supervise them if they have preliminary success, and so on."

Finally, Stalin raised a glass to congratulate the graduates of the military school and hoped that they would be successful in national defense organization and leadership. (TASS, 6th)

End of the Italy-Austria-Hungary Conference; Obstacles to the Rome Conference Removed; Hungary Agrees Not to Raise Demands for Military Reorganization and Treaty Revision; Agreement Reached on the Danube River Convention to Facilitate

Small Entente Foreign Ministers to Meet in Rome Next Tuesday

Venice—The foreign ministers of Italy, Hungary, and Austria held a conference here last Saturday and Sunday to discuss far-reaching European affairs. It concluded today. According to a press release, the three countries reached a consensus during the conference and paid special attention to the Torri del Lago talks to be held in Rome on May 20, in order to implement the Rome Protocol signed by France and Italy on January 7. The main provision of the Protocol is to guarantee Austria's independence with a Central European Convention, which will be discussed at the Rome talks. Participants include representatives from nine countries: France, Italy, Austria, Germany, Hungary, Poland, Romania, Yugoslavia, and Czechoslovakia. (Reuters, 6th)

Venice—The Torri del Lago Conference will be held next month in Rome. The preparatory meeting of representatives from Italy, Austria, and Hungary concluded this afternoon. An official statement said that the negotiations were conducted in an atmosphere of amity and cooperation, and that all key points had been resolved and the goals of the three governments were fully aligned. Political circles here indicated that future developments will be determined by other countries, especially the Little Entente. Representatives of the Little Entente countries will convene a preliminary meeting in the Romanian capital on May 14 to discuss the Danube River issue. According to reliable sources, the Hungarian demands for military equality and antagonism towards the Little Entente are major obstacles to the ultimate success of the Rome Conference. Hungary has now agreed to participate in the Torri del Lago Conference, but reserves the right to refuse to sign the Torri del Lago Convention. It is reported that Hungarian Foreign Minister Kánya declared that Hungary is prepared to sign a military treaty guaranteeing the independence of Austria and Hungary, but does not want to fight against Germany under any circumstances. It is heard that Hungary is now seeking to obtain the right to implement conscription, cancel accusations unfavorable to Hungary in the Marseille assassination case, and not to restrict Austria's right to revise the borders stipulated in the Treaty of Versailles in the non-interference agreement with Austria, as conditions for participating in the Danube River Convention. (National News Agency, 6th)

Venice, Italy—Representatives from Italy, Austria, and Hungary held their third meeting today, which concluded in the afternoon. After today's meeting, the prospects for the nine-nation conference in Rome seem to be gradually improving. An official press release stated that Italy, Austria, and Hungary, in a spirit of friendship and cooperation, jointly held talks and proved that the goals of the three countries were completely consistent. They firmly believe that the preparatory work currently underway is sufficient to facilitate understanding among the countries involved in the Danube River Conference. The main result of the three-nation meeting was to enable Hungary to participate in the Danube River Conference. Hungary requested that the issues of military equality and the possibility of revising the treaty be considered in conjunction with the Torri del Lago Convention. After discussions at the Venice Conference, it seems that an agreement has been reached that the issue of military rearmament will not be discussed at the Rome Conference. However, Italy is solely responsible for suggesting that a special meeting be convened separately after the Rome Conference to discuss the issue of military rearmament. It is generally believed that Italy's attitude towards the Hungarian issue will not bind other countries, and the purpose of the non-interference agreement is solely to guarantee Austria's independence and prevent Austria's political system from being changed due to foreign propaganda. Therefore, after the non-interference agreement is signed, it will be even more difficult to restore the Habsburg dynasty. This should be satisfactory to the countries of the Little Entente. Regarding economic issues, it is reported that at the Venice Conference, Italy and Austria have agreed to renew trade agreements with Hungary and purchase Hungarian wheat. (Havas, 6th)

Budapest, Hungary—It is generally believed that at the Venice three-nation conference, the Hungarian government has disregarded all difficulties and made all kinds of concessions to the maximum extent, but hopes that the three Little Entente countries will also make similar concessions at the Rome Conference. According to unconfirmed official sources, Hungary has agreed that if the countries concerned recognize that, in accordance with Article 19 of the Covenant of the League of Nations (which stipulates that outdated treaties may be submitted to the League of Nations Assembly for review by member states), certain territorial clauses in the treaty with Hungary may be amended in the future, Hungary will not raise the issue of treaty revision at the Rome Conference. (Havas, 6th)

(Rome) In order to ensure the success of the Torri del Lago Conference, the Italian government has decided to follow the resolutions of the Italy-Austria-Hungary conference in Venice and invite the foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries to Rome for the same preparatory meeting, so that the important issues to be discussed at the Danube River Conference can first be adequately understood. The date of this preparatory meeting has not yet been determined, but it will probably be held after the foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries meet in the Romanian capital on May 14. (National News Agency, 7th)

(Paris) News from Venice received by various newspapers here mostly stated that Italy will issue a formal declaration before the Danube River Conference, recognizing Hungary's military equality, but the way to achieve this will be through diplomatic negotiations. Furthermore, several newspapers believe that the reason why the joint declaration of the three countries after the Venice Conference did not mention maintaining the status quo in Central Europe is that they did not want to block Hungary from achieving its treaty revision claims through peaceful means. All parties in France are extremely satisfied with the results of the Venice Conference. (National News Agency, 7th)

Japan Pays Attention to US Shipbuilding Plan; Next Year's Japanese Army Budget to Exceed 500 Million Yen

(Tokyo) The US House of Representatives has approved the budget for 1935 to 1936, which includes funds for building new warships, and is currently under consideration by the Senate. The Japanese naval authorities are paying attention to the Senate's attitude. If this budget is passed by the Senate, the United States will begin building 24 new warships next year. Because 44 ships were already built last year, the United States will build 68 ships in two years, which is several times the number of ships built by Britain, France, and Italy. The main points of its shipbuilding plan are recorded as follows: Those started last year: (1) Two aircraft carriers, (2) Seven Class B cruisers, (3) Twenty-nine destroyers, (4) Six submarines, a total of 44 ships. Those to be started this year: (1) Fifteen destroyers, (2) Six minelayers, a total of 24 ships. In addition, there is one Class A cruiser stipulated by the treaty. Comparing this with the shipbuilding situation of Britain, France, and Italy, it can be seen how large the plan is.

Britain

Those started in fiscal year 1934: One aircraft carrier, four Class B cruisers, nine destroyers, two submarines, a total of 17 ships. Those started in fiscal year 1935: Three Class B cruisers, nine destroyers, three submarines, a total of 15 ships.

France

Those started in fiscal year 1934: One capital ship, one destroyer, six patrol ships, a total of nine ships. Those started in fiscal year 1935: One destroyer, three submarines, a total of four ships.

Italy

Two capital ships. (Japan United Press, 7th)

(Tokyo) The Okada Cabinet has now begun to study the guiding principles for compiling next year's budget. The core of next year's budget is the Army's Capital Improvement Fee (i.e., the so-called Second National Defense Enhancement Fee). The balance of the first Capital Improvement Fee after next year is only 27 million yen, but judging from the current international situation, the Capital Improvement Fee for the next two or three years must be at least 120 million yen each year. According to the Army's estimate of next year's budget, its content is as follows: (1) Standard budget of 280 million yen, divided into a general budget of 200 million yen, an emergency preparedness fee for air defense forces of 68 million yen, a fee for improving various systems of 6 million yen, a fee for reforming education and training of 3 million yen, and a fee for reorganizing the Korean garrison division of 4 million yen. (2) Capital Improvement Fee of 100 million yen. (3) Manchurian Incident Fee of 140 million yen. (4) Several other new budgets. From this perspective, next year's Army budget will exceed 500 million yen. (Japan United Press, 7th)

US Supreme Court Rules Railroad Pension Act Unconstitutional

(Washington) The US Supreme Court today declared the Railroad Pension Act unconstitutional. This ruling is related to more than one million railway workers. Justice Roberts expressed the court's opinion, saying that this act is invalid because it violates due process of law. This act has no purpose or effect of regulating commerce and exceeds the power of Congress. It is said that this statement has established a principle, and the court's ruling on the National Recovery Act in the future may be affected by this. Chief Justice Hughes dissented alone, saying that this ruling deviates from sound principles and places inappropriate restrictions on the Constitution's commerce clause. One provision of the act made it enforceable on all interstate carriers, even those not directly related to interstate trade. This section was particularly disliked by the court. The court believed that the act could not be severed, so the court had no choice but to recognize that the entire act was invalid. Furthermore, this act was not designed to regulate interstate trade, so it is also invalid for this reason. In addition, the court also pointed out that railway workers who have voluntarily left freight service, or who have been dismissed for incompetence or misconduct, and those who have served for a full term and are naturally dismissed, must all be given a pension. When Roosevelt signed this act last June, he said that this case was hastily drafted and that the next Congress would have to make various revisions to it. In this court ruling, five justices agreed and four opposed. If this act was supported by the court, railway companies would increase their office expenses by 60 million yuan each year. (Reuters, 6th)

Page 7

Overseas Chinese in Dutch East Indies Receive Unequal Legal Treatment; Blow to Emigration; Those Concerned with Overseas Chinese Affairs Should Not Overlook This

(Nanjing) The Hague Correspondence: The Dutch East Indies is where most of our overseas Chinese gather, with a population of about 1.2 million. The businesses they run occupy an important position in the area, and the interconnected relationship with domestic economic institutions is also inseparable. For several years, the central government has repeatedly dispatched high-ranking officials to conduct inspections, with the aim of enhancing commerce and economy between China and the Dutch East Indies. The relationship between the two countries will become increasingly complex, and the various issues between the two countries must be resolved quickly. The most important issues are the Dutch East Indies' restrictions on immigration and the legal status of overseas Chinese. The origins of these two issues are summarized as follows: (1) Immigration Restriction Issue: Since 1933, the Dutch East Indies has been affected by the world economic crisis. The year before last, it proposed immigration restriction measures to provide relief. The content of the measures is: 1. The total number of immigrants entering each year must be specified. 2. If the number of entries is less than the quota, the number of immigrants may be increased by each ethnic group, but it must not exceed one-tenth of the total number of immigrants of that ethnic group into the Dutch East Indies in the ten consecutive years before the implementation of the new regulations. 3. After the quota limit is reached, only ethnic groups whose number of immigrants has not reached the limit are allowed to continue to immigrate. When this regulation was submitted to the Dutch East Indies National Assembly, our country believed that if this article were passed and implemented, not only would our country's emigration policy be hit, but also the economic status of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies would be fatally shaken. If based on the new immigration law, the legal quota for Chinese to immigrate each year is only 800 people. The former acting representative of our embassy in the Netherlands sent a note to the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs in the same year, urging it to consider not allowing the regulations to be passed hastily. More than 30 Chinese chambers of commerce in the Dutch East Indies also jointly petitioned the Dutch Governor, hoping that he would find a way to revoke or amend it. The Dutch East Indies National Assembly passed the regulations and the Dutch government approved them. After Minister Jin Wensi took office, he repeatedly negotiated with the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs and urged it to respond as soon as possible. On December 14, 1933, he once again sent a note to the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs, explaining our government's views and declaring the reservation of the right to raise this issue again in the future. This note was sent by the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the Ministry of Colonies and forwarded to the Dutch East Indies Governor. After the new regulations were implemented in January 1934, according to the report of our country's Consulate General in Batavia, based on the report of the Dutch East Indies Immigration Bureau, the number of Chinese entering the country in the past eleven months of last year has reached 6,771, which is more than the number of Chinese entering in 1932 (5,980 people) and 1933 (4,954 people). From this point of view, although the Dutch government has not formally recognized our country's demands in writing, it has in fact given us full sympathy. This year, the Dutch East Indies government explicitly announced that the total number of foreign nationals entering the country is still 12,000. It is still unknown whether the number of Chinese entering the country can maintain the original number of last year. Those concerned with overseas Chinese affairs should not overlook this. (2) Legal Treatment Issue: Article 163 of the Dutch East Indies Constitution stipulates that all Europeans and Japanese are collectively referred to as Europeans, while Chinese and Arabs are referred to as Eastern Foreigners. There are many points of unequal treatment. For example, European cases are tried by judges, but this is not the case for Eastern Foreigners. In criminal suspected cases, Europeans are arrested by the court, while Eastern Foreigners are detained by the police station. The facilities in European detention centers and prisons, and the treatment they enjoy, are superior to those of Eastern Foreigners. Our overseas Chinese have endured all this unequal treatment. When our national government established its capital in Nanjing, the former Dutch Governor (i.e., the current Foreign Minister Graeff) declared at the opening of the 11th regular meeting of the National Assembly on June 15, 1929, that the Chinese national government would promulgate family law on January 1 of the following year. If it can be implemented, the legal treatment of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies can be equal to that of the Dutch. However, our laws on family and inheritance have been implemented successively since May 5 of the 20th year (i.e., 1931), but the legal treatment of our overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies has never been equal to that of Europeans, Americans, and Japanese. Our embassy in the Netherlands has continued to negotiate with the Dutch government. On May 2 of last year, the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent a note to our embassy stating that the legal status of overseas Chinese, except for aspects of criminal procedure law that still need to be improved, can be treated equally with Europeans in terms of civil law, civil procedure law, commercial law, and criminal law. The legal treatment of overseas Chinese has indeed made progress, but to obtain the most satisfactory results, more efforts are still needed. (Central News Agency, 7th)

International Commercial Telegram

Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters, May 7th

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold price decreased by 5.5 pence this morning to 143 shillings and 7.5 pence.

London Silver: The London silver market was quiet. The spot price was 33.75 pence, and the futures price was 33.9375 pence, both up 1/875. There were speculators buying and selling in the morning, with moderate trading. The market closed steadily.

Mount Real Silver: The Mount Real silver market price was quite stable. The market price opened slightly higher today, expressing sympathy with the rise in London.

Exchange Rates

GBP/USD: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The pound was stable. The GBP/USD exchange rate opened at $4.8475, lower by 1/875 compared to the closing rate on Saturday and Sunday in New York and London. The exchange rate fluctuated in the morning. At 2:00 PM, the price was $4.84375, lower by 3/875 compared to the opening rate this morning.

GBP/FRF: The GBP/FRF exchange rate opened higher by 19 centimes at 73.56 francs. It rose slightly at 11:00 AM to 73.57 francs, then fell. At 1:00 PM, the price was 72.46 francs, lower by 10 centimes compared to the opening rate.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened slightly higher today. Generally, trading was very thin, but sentiment remained strong. The opening price remained unchanged. Foreigners apparently sold, and brokers slightly bought. There have been recent heavy rains in many cotton-producing areas.

US Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was relatively loose today. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings and 6.75 pence, down 2.5.

UK Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was also loose. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 6.46, lower by 4 points compared to the closing on Saturday and Sunday.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened firmly, due to reports of insufficient rainfall in the southwest. Later, due to news of more favorable weather, wheat prices loosened slightly.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was stable today. At noon, the trading price for July and September futures was 5.75 pence, higher by 0.0625 compared to the last closing price.

New York: The New York rubber market was thin, with sluggish trading, due to the uncertain outcome of the automobile industry strike.

Guangdong Province Promotes Local Autonomy

Focuses on training people to exercise the four rights, land surveying and population census nearing completion

Guangzhou Correspondence. Since the promulgation of local autonomy laws and regulations in July 1931, Guangdong Province has dispatched local autonomy assistant officers from the Department of Civil Affairs to assist various counties in preparing for local autonomy. Over the past four years, 95 county and municipal councils have been established, as well as 773 district offices, 12,546 township offices, and 688 town offices throughout the province. Neighborhood offices have not yet been counted. The Provincial Council was also established on August 15, 1934. However, due to the lack of education or economic backwardness in Ling Shui, Ganen, Changjiang, and Daoxian counties, the progress of local autonomy is relatively low. Other counties have made considerable progress. However, the first step in preparing for local autonomy is to train the people to exercise the four rights. If the people do not understand the exercise of the four rights, they may be easily manipulated by local gentry. Therefore, this training should be carried out in a gradual manner, starting with the training of cadres. Therefore, since July 1932, the Guangdong Provincial Local Autonomy Staff Training Institute was established to transfer autonomy personnel from district offices in various counties and cities to the institute for training. After completing their studies, they are sent back to serve, so as not to overstep or make mistakes. Subsequently, county councilor training classes were opened, and councilors from various counties and cities were drawn to attend training, so as to ensure that councilors from various counties and cities have a further understanding of the principles of self-governance. Furthermore, the rotational training method for autonomy personnel in counties, townships, and villages was revised, and autonomy trainers were dispatched to various counties to train the heads and deputy heads of townships and villages in various counties on a rotational basis. Up to now, the Local Autonomy Staff Training Institute has gone through ten terms, with approximately over 2,000 graduates. The County Councilor Training Class has also gone through two sessions, with approximately over 100 graduates. As for the training of the heads and deputy heads of townships and villages in various counties, the counties that have completed the training include Sanshui, Dongguan, Shunde, Jieyang, Boluo, Lingshan, Lianjiang, Xinyi, Guangning, Sihui, Gaoyao, Luoding, Qiongshan, Danxian, and other counties. Future work will continue. After the autonomy personnel at all levels in each county and city have received considerable training, ordinary people will be trained to understand the exercise of the four rights, so that they can gradually establish a model of local autonomy. As for the population census, a provincial population census implementation plan and implementation procedures have been formulated. In 1933, all counties were ordered to set up population census offices. October 1, 1933, was the date for the provincial population census. Up to now, more than 50 counties have completed the investigation and will soon be able to conclude the announcement. Once the investigation is completed, household registration control zones can be established in various counties in accordance with the Household Registration Law, with the heads of townships and villages concurrently serving as household registration directors to carry out personnel registration. Land surveying is also progressing gradually. Initially, the Provincial Government established the Guangdong Provincial Land Administration Personnel Training Institute to recruit and train students. After graduation, land surveying teams were formed. There have now been five graduating classes, and 44 surveying teams have been formed successively, which have been sent to Nanhai, Panyu, Xinhui, Taishan, Hepu, Gaoyao, Shunde, Dongguan, Qingyuan, [unclear]ping, Maoming, Shantou, and other counties and cities to carry out surveying. At present, a total of 354,504 houses and 850,059 mu of farmland have been surveyed. Future work will continue. Once the surveying of each county is completed, land registration can be compiled, and land taxes can be abolished and land taxes can be levied. The equalization of land ownership, which is a part of the Principle of People's Livelihood, can also be gradually implemented. Other aspects, such as the reorganization of local guards and the construction of roads, are also progressing. Recently, in order to promote the early completion of local autonomy, the Provincial Government has also revised the Guangdong Province Township and Village Autonomy Training Officer Dispatch Method and added township and village autonomy training officers, who are dispatched from graduates of the political advanced studies class of the Guangdong Military and Political School. The province is divided into five regions: Central, Eastern, Southern, Northwestern, and Qiongyai. Except for the counties that have been convened and trained by previous autonomy trainers, training officers will be assigned to the counties that have not been trained. Four groups are assigned to the central region, six groups to the eastern region, four groups to the northwest region, four groups to the southern region, and two groups to the Qiongyai region, with each group having more than 10 people or 8 or 9 people, and each group having a group leader and a deputy group leader. The work of the trainers includes: (1) training township and village autonomy personnel; (2) examining the actual situation of township and village autonomy; (3) publicizing the essentials of local autonomy. They can also provide guidance and supervision on other autonomy matters within their scope when necessary. The subjects for training autonomy personnel include: (A) Party ideology; (B) General principles of local autonomy; (C) Current autonomy laws and regulations; (D) Methods of exercising the four rights; (E) Elementary principles of people's rights. Additional subjects can be added as necessary. When trainers arrive in each county, they are divided into several small teams, with at least four people in each team, and they train in rotation. When they arrive at a district office, they convene the heads and deputy heads of the townships and villages under its jurisdiction for training. The training time is one week, and it can be extended if necessary. The training situation is reported at any time. If there are any difficult problems, the group leader convenes a meeting of group members to solve them, and a report must be submitted. Trainers receive food and lodging expenses and must not accept gifts from the public. The training methods and service regulations are roughly as described above. The main point is to promote local autonomy by starting with training in order to cultivate good autonomy personnel, which lies in engaging in practical work.

Record of the Capture and Execution of the Bandit Leader "Black Face Zhang" in Southern Shandong

Special Detectives from Shandong Arrest Zhang in Anhui; Executed After Interrogation by Han Fuqu

According to dispatches from Southern Shandong, Zhang Heilian (Black Face Zhang), a notorious bandit leader in the Yinan and Southern Shandong area, rivaling Liu Guitang and known as one of the "Two Blacks of Southern Shandong," once led tens of thousands of men, occupying the border area between Jiangsu, Shandong, and Anhui provinces for nearly two years. Almost all the bandit leaders of Southern Shandong came from his ranks, considering themselves his followers. The counties of Teng, Yi, Lin, Cao, Ju, Yi, and Ri in Southern Shandong were all within his sphere of influence, earning him the title "King of Ten Thousand Mountains." When Liu Guitang was incorporated into the government forces in 1932, Xia Ziming was sent to negotiate Zhang Heilian's incorporation as well. He boarded a train in Teng County, but when the train reached Liangbudian Station, Zhang rebelled again, getting off the train midway and escaping into Mount Culaishan, then to Mount Mengshan. His subordinates scattered. In recent years, the Shandong authorities had been rigorously pursuing him. Zhang Heilian then left Shandong with a gun, hiding in Xinmaqiao, 70 li north of the city of Anhui, disguised as a farmer. He dug the ground, collected manure, feigned deafness and acted foolish. Liu Yaoting, the leader of the Third Route Special Detective Team, upon discovering Zhang's hiding place, led his detectives there himself to make the arrest. After four hours of searching, they captured Zhang and his bandit followers Sun Yewen and Liu Yuzhen in the area. At 8:00 AM on the fifth day, they arrived in Jinan. A major threat of many years was eliminated in one swoop, bringing great joy to the hearts of the people. The details of what happened are described below:

After Zhang Heilian's attempted incorporation failed in 1932 and he fled to Mount Mengshan, his subordinates died, scattered, deserted, and gradually disappeared. Feeling that the environment was unfavorable, he left Shandong for Anhui. He had four different residences. Zhang's father, Zhang Yunrang, lived in Pukou. Zhang's sister and his adopted son lived in a coal kiln in Huaiyuan County, 90 li west of Bengbu. Zhang's wife and daughters lived in Xinzhi, Anhui. Zhang himself traveled around, his whereabouts uncertain. Recently, he lived in the home of his adopted son, the bandit Sun Jiwen, in Xinmaqiao, 70 li north of Bengbu. Sun made a living by building houses and selling oil. Zhang lived there, disguised as a farmer, collecting manure every day, and acting crazy. The villagers called him a fool. Another bandit, Liu Yuzhen, also lived in the area, nicknamed "Pockmarked Liu the Second," living beyond the reach of the law. This was reported to Liu Yaoting, the leader of the Third Route Special Detective Team, who, at 8:50 PM one evening, took the director, Cai Licen, and four detectives, along with an informant, from Jinan to make the arrest. After arriving in Bengbu, they secretly investigated and learned that Zhang Heilian had recently moved from Xinji to Xinmaqiao. On the night of the third day, they departed from Bengbu Station and arrived in Xinmaqiao at 1:00 AM on the fourth day. After contacting the local security team in advance, the team surrounded Xinmaqiao. At that time, they went to the home of Zhang's adopted son, Sun Yewen. The informant went forward to knock on the door, falsely claiming to be Sun's brother-in-law, sent to deliver a message saying that the officials had sent people to arrest the "commander" (Zhang Heilian) and ordering him to prepare to escape. Sun Yewen was also afraid that it was a trick. After listening carefully, he realized that there were indeed the sounds of soldiers moving outside the village (the security team was indeed in the village). Sun hurriedly went to where the bandit was staying. The messenger pushed the door open. At this time, Liu Yaoting and the hidden detectives also followed. Liu shined a flashlight into the room, illuminating the bed, and the informant pointed to the person in the bed as Zhang Heilian. The detectives then pointed their guns at him, effortlessly arresting Zhang. His adopted son, Sun Yewen, was also captured at the same time. Zhang still denied being a bandit. Liu Yaoting falsely claimed that Liu "Pockmarked" (who had once been Zhang's regimental commander) had used 500 silver dollars to expose him. Knowing that he could not hide the truth, Zhang finally admitted that he was Zhang Heilian and said that Liu "Pockmarked the Second" was also a bandit living in the same village. Zhang then led the detectives to Liu "Pockmarked"'s house, where they captured Liu. Then, Liu Yaoting personally escorted them to the station. Zhang's wife and three daughters all came to the station to see him off. His wife cried, and his daughters cried too. The oldest daughter was over ten years old, and the younger ones were all under ten. They were all in tears, sobbing uncontrollably. Zhang told his wife and daughters, "You don't have to cry. I'm not coming back this time. Do whatever you have to do." His wife also said to Zhang, "You didn't bring any money. I borrowed for half a day in the village and couldn't borrow any." Zhang said, "I don't need money," and earnestly told his daughters, "You must be filial to your mother and listen to her." At this point, the detective team escorted Zhang onto a freight car heading north. After arriving in Xuzhou, they transferred to the Jinpu Line Train No. 22 and arrived in Jinan at 8:00 AM on the fifth day. They were then taken by car to the headquarters of the Special Detective Team on Xiaowei Sixth Road. At 9:00 AM, Liu went to the provincial government to report to Han Fuqu. (To be continued)

Autopsy in Husband's Murder of Wife Case

Yan Genbao, a resident of Dahegang Township in Guanxiang, killed his wife, Shen, with a sharp blade because he resented her infidelity. Yan Genbao was arrested on the spot. The details have already been reported in yesterday's telegram in this newspaper. It is now known that the Procuratorate of the District Court sent Prosecutor Shen to conduct an autopsy in the township yesterday (the seventh) morning, along with a coroner. It was determined that the deceased, Shen, had been stabbed three times with a knife while alive, resulting in death. The family was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial and await further investigation. The murderer, Yan Genbao, was also sent to the District Procuratorate by the Public Security Bureau yesterday (the seventh). After questioning by Prosecutor Shen, he was immediately detained.

Wuxi Suzhou Tax Committee Holds Meeting in Wuxi

Resolution to Strengthen Public Security Forces

The Wuxi County Public Security Bureau has recently experienced frequent cases in the urban area. The police force is too weak. Once something happens, they are unable to handle everything. They urgently need to strengthen their forces and purchase more guns and ammunition for defense. They also need to install telephones to facilitate communication. The bicycle fleet of the patrol team is old and damaged and cannot be repaired. They should also be replaced to facilitate duty. All of this was reported to the county government. It was discussed at the County Affairs Council meeting yesterday. It was resolved to approve the purchase of twelve bicycles, sixty White Lingham pistols, and six thousand bullets. As for the installation of telephones, it was decided to first install them at the five city gates of the east, west, south, north, and Guangfu, and at the eight ferries, including Du Gang. A special request was submitted to use the surplus funds from the 12th fiscal year and to add telephone operating expenses.

Changshu Rickshaw Pullers' Strike Quickly Resolved

More than 500 rickshaw pullers in the county suddenly went on strike on the morning of the fifth, forming a team to petition the Party and government agencies. The reason was that recently, some rickshaw puller foremen organized a union, requiring each rickshaw puller to donate five copper coins per day as membership fees. Recently, the rickshaw pullers have had little business, making it difficult to bear the burden. Furthermore, the large amount of money donated to the union was useless and only used by a few people. Therefore, they rebelled together. After persuasion by the Party and government agencies and the guarantee that the donation would be canceled, the result was very satisfactory. Some of the rickshaw pullers resumed work at 3:00 PM.

Changzhou Student Crushed to Death at Wansheng Iron Factory

Shu Wanniu, an eighteen-year-old student from the Wuyi Xinximen Road Wansheng Iron Factory, a resident of Dong'an Township, Ninth District, was working the night shift at the factory at around 8:00 PM on the evening of the sixth. He accidentally touched the machine shaft, resulting in both legs being crushed and the brain also being crushed, with fluids pouring out. The factory manager, realizing the accident, immediately stopped the machine and sent the injured person to Wujin Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of the injuries, he died soon after.

All sectors of Nantong will hold a public memorial on the 59th National Humiliation Day at Langshan Road for Cao Ding, a martyr of the Ming Dynasty who died fighting Japanese pirates. Hangzhou Detective Team Captures Bracelet Robber

Zhongxing, the four-year-old son of Zhu Songyuan, the director of Gongbu Xinda Transport Company, was crying alone along the Datong Canal yesterday (the sixth) evening. Shen Jiang, a boatman of the company, noticed him and took him home. While walking along the river near Majiaqiao, a bandit suddenly came from behind and robbed the silver bracelet from the child's wrist. At that time, Hong Jingru, the captain of the detective squad stationed in Gongbu of the Public Security Bureau, and squad member Li Qishu passed by and, after hearing the news, gave chase. They captured a robber named Ding Baoshan. The victim and the child confirmed that he was the robber. He has been sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Haimen Villager Shot to Death by Thieves

Mao Xianrong, a villager near Hezhen in the Fifth District, was moderately wealthy. At around 9:00 PM the day before yesterday, more than ten bandits suddenly broke into his house, looting extensively. They stole more than 30 yuan and more than ten pieces of clothing. Mao's son, Shimin, who is studying at the Nengren Middle School in the county, reported to the county government yesterday after receiving the news. Local News

Banks Increase Lending to Industry and Commerce; Member Banks Increase Commitment by 500,000 Yuan; Money Trade Association to Meet on 10th to Discuss

According to the Central News Agency, after the amount of 5 million yuan for lending to industry and commerce was determined, the Bankers Association held a meeting to discuss it and recommended Chairman Ye and Wang to report to Finance Minister Kong. The association has agreed to raise 1.5 million yuan and will contact the major banks separately. The Money Trade Association is scheduled to meet on the 10th to discuss it. The details are as follows:

Three Banks Comply with Order to Undertake

After Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi planned to change the method of underwriting the 5 million yuan loan to industry and commerce to 1 million yuan from the Central Bank, 1 million yuan from the Bank of China, 500,000 yuan from the Bank of Communications, 1.5 million yuan from the Bankers Association, and 2 million yuan from the Money Trade Association, the Central Bank has complied, handled by Xi Demao, the manager of the Business Bureau. The Bank of China will immediately hand over the 1 million yuan to Bei Songsun, the manager of the Shanghai branch. The Bank of Communications will add 100,000 yuan to the already committed 400,000 yuan and hand it over to Zhang Peishen, the manager of the Business Bureau. (New Life News Agency)

Bankers Association to Issue Notice

The amount of 5 million yuan for lending to industry and commerce has been generally decided. The Bankers Association convened an executive committee meeting the day before yesterday and invited representatives from member banks to attend. As a result of the discussion, the association decided to raise 1 million yuan and asked the banks that had already committed to double their commitment. Those who had not committed or committed less were asked to increase their commitment. The association has drafted a letter based on the proceedings of the meeting and will notify the member banks. After the letter is finalized and signed by the standing committee members, it will be issued today. (Central News Agency below)

Chairman Ye and Wang Report to Kong

As for the remaining 500,000 yuan, the association originally planned to ask Finance Minister Kong to contact non-member banks to commit. There are still 50 to 60 banks in Shanghai that have not joined the association. Expanding the scope would make it easier to raise funds. Therefore, it was decided, and the two standing committee members, Ye Fuxiao and Wang Yansong, were recommended to report to Finance Minister Kong and state this intention. Ye and Wang went to the Central Bank after the meeting to report to Kong.

500,000 Yuan Successfully Negotiated

According to a written reply from Ye to a reporter from the Central News Agency, "As a result of reporting to Kong, the remaining 500,000 yuan will still be committed by member banks." According to Lin Kanghou, the secretary-general of the Bankers Association, he received a telegram from Ye stating that Finance Minister Kong found it cumbersome and difficult to conduct separate negotiations with non-member banks, and this matter could not be delayed any longer. Therefore, the Bankers Association was asked to try its best to raise the funds. The Bankers Association will fulfill the purpose of the Ministry of Finance to rescue industry and commerce and practice the function of regulating finance. It has now agreed to find a way to raise funds again. However, some banks with less capital have already committed as much as they can. Therefore, the association has decided to have the responsible person negotiate with banks with strong capital to increase their commitment in order to raise the funds as soon as possible.

Money Trade Association Schedules Meeting to Discuss

The Money Trade Association had previously resolved to participate in the commitment of 250,000 yuan, which would be shared equally by the member money shops. However, Finance Minister Kong requested an increase to 1 million yuan. Although the chairman of the association, Qin Runqing, accepted at the time, the amount was four times the original amount and required the approval of all members. It is reported that the Executive Committee meeting originally scheduled for the 10th (Friday) will invite representatives from the member money shops to attend in order to report on the proceedings of the tea party attended by Finance Minister Kong and to discuss ways to collect the funds.

Foreign Reports Are Not True

Summer House Tax Scheduled to Be Collected in the City

The Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, in order to improve the system of collecting house taxes, submitted a request to the municipal government for approval from the central government to amend Articles 13 and 16 of the House Tax Regulations. For all commercial and residential households with quarterly house taxes of 10 yuan or more, the tax collection office will issue a notice before the start of each quarter. After receiving the notice, taxpayers must bring the notice to the tax collection office to pay within 15 days. If they have not paid within 10 days after the deadline, staff will be sent to collect the tax at their door, and a penalty of 2% of the tax due will be added. For households with house taxes of less than 10 yuan, staff will still be sent by the tax collection office to collect the tax. Those who wish to pay at the tax collection office themselves may do so. The house tax for this summer is scheduled to begin on May 16.

International Radio Station Expands Facilities

Zhenru Transmitting Station Adds High-Power Transmitter; Shanghai-Guangdong-Hankou Wireless Telephone Equipment to Be Completed Soon; Expansion of Teleprinter Telephone Receiving and Sending Business Report Equipment

The Shanghai Ministry of Communications International Radio Station has its general management office and central receiving and sending office in the Sassoon Building at the Renji Road intersection, and its transmitting stations are located in Zhenru and Fenglinqiao. Due to the station's thriving southern business and a large increase in external communication lines, the original equipment was insufficient. A 20-40 kilowatt shortwave transmitter was purchased from the United States. The station staff rushed to install the equipment, and the Ministry of Communications ordered Yu Ruxin and Shen Shuren to come to Shanghai to inspect and accept the equipment. It is now officially in use, which has greatly facilitated the station's communication with Europe and the United States. The Ministry of Communications originally designated the Shanghai-Guangdong-Hankou wireless telephone communication affairs to be under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, but for the sake of economic position and convenience in engineering, the Shanghai portion of the equipment was attached to the internal facilities of the International Radio Station and ordered to be installed by the station. This is now generally ready. However, the construction of 16 iron towers in Zhenru and Liuhang to prepare for hanging antennas is still in progress due to the large scale of the project.

In order to improve the speed of telegraph delivery for various merchants in the city, the station installed a telephone line exchange in the central receiving and sending room of the station at Renji Road, Shanghai, so that major merchants can use teleprinters or telephones to directly contact the station's telegraph room. A single room is used to allow telegrams to be received and sent as soon as possible, which is extremely fast. Currently, the number of major merchants applying to the station to use this dedicated line is increasing daily, and they are all praising its convenience.

International Problems Research Association: Yesterday's Speech on the Truth of Anti-Chinese Sentiment in Siam, Suppression of Education and Ruin of Industry and Commerce, No Stone Left Unturned; Miscellaneous Grain Association to Discuss Boycott of Siamese Rice Today

To clarify the truth about the Siamese government's active anti-Chinese sentiment and the plight of overseas Chinese, and to show support, the International Problems Research Association invited a certain petition representative of overseas Chinese returning from Siam to make a detailed report at the Bank Club at 5:30 PM yesterday. More than 30 people attended, including Cao Yunxiang, Guo Bingwen, Shen Xinqing, Chen Liting, Zhang Xianglin, He Dekui, Cheng Haifeng, Tu Youyu, etc. Chen Liting presided over the meeting.

Abuse of Overseas Chinese: Various Harsh Regulations

Mr. So-and-so first stated that after the completion of the Siamese constitutional government, they have been making every effort to assimilate overseas Chinese. All measures are aimed at making the more than 3 million overseas Chinese in Siam, who account for a quarter of the total population of Siam, completely become Siamese people. Next, he elaborated on (1) amending the immigration law to reject illiterate people from entering, restricting the southward migration of laborers and women, and arranging for overseas Chinese in Siam to marry Siamese women so that their offspring will forget their motherland; (2) suppressing overseas Chinese education, having already closed more than 60 overseas Chinese schools one after another, restricting those under the age of 14 to study in Siamese public schools and forbidding them from learning Chinese; (3) ruining overseas Chinese industry and commerce by heavily taxing various industries, attempting to reclaim the alcohol industry to be managed by the government, and recently planning to control foreign exchange, so that overseas Chinese cannot remit money back to their country; (4) the newly promulgated fisheries regulations limit fishing licenses to Siamese citizens, so overseas Chinese fishermen have to have their Siamese wives obtain the licenses, and the Siamese government also issued regulations restricting the workers employed by fishermen to be 75% Siamese; (5) children of overseas Chinese under the age of 14 are in the period of compulsory education and are not allowed to leave Siam, and upon reaching the age of 18, they are subject to military service and must serve, otherwise they will be punished for evading military service. This regulation was originally scheduled to be implemented on April 1, but because many overseas Chinese planned to send their children back to their home country, the Siamese government temporarily postponed it and will implement it near September 1.

Banning Siamese Rice: No Harm to Overseas Chinese

Subsequently, Mr. He Dekui asked whether boycotting Siamese rice would affect overseas Chinese in Siam. Mr. So-and-so replied that most overseas Chinese in Siam are engaged in industry and commerce and do not grow grains. Although there are more than 100 rice mills, most also operate other businesses. Recently, Siamese rice mills have been losing money due to farmers hoarding rice. If our country stops dealing in Siamese rice, it will not only not harm overseas Chinese who run rice mills, but it can also reduce losses. The farmers are the ones who will suffer the losses, and the current rulers of Siam, who want to gain the trust of the farmers, are deeply afraid of losing the support of the people and shaking their political position, so they will definitely be willing to sign a trade treaty with our country, and so on. The association decided to submit the aid plan to the board of directors for discussion.

Miscellaneous Grain Association to Discuss Today

Regarding the matter of Siam discriminating against overseas Chinese, the Overseas Chinese United Association put forward opinions, requesting the rice industry in this city to ban the import of Siamese rice to boycott and urge the Siamese government authorities to pay attention. They also sent representatives to meet with Mr. Gu Xinyi the day before yesterday to inquire about his opinions. The Miscellaneous Grain Association specifically scheduled a meeting to be held at 4:00 PM today to discuss the matter and plan to send a telegram to the Siamese government requesting improvement in the treatment of overseas Chinese. The above telegram is currently being drafted and will be submitted for discussion at today's meeting. It will be sent after it is passed, it is said.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submits to the Ministry of Finance: Requesting Exemption from Export Tax on Chinese Medicine

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a memorial to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating, "Regarding the matter of submitting a petition, according to a letter from the Pharmaceutical Industry Guild dated the 4th of this month, our country's medicinal materials are produced in Sichuan, Yunnan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Henan, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Guangxi, and other provinces. They are first collected in cities and then transported to other places. Shanghai is a commercial hub, so medicinal materials from various places must first be concentrated and then transferred. Therefore, the number of medicinal herbs re-exported and exported in a year is quite large. Now, when the government is formulating tax regulations, the various re-export taxes have been exempted from June 1, while the various export taxes are still under review. According to the regulations, there is a distinction between tax exemption and no tax exemption. However, for our medicinal materials, there is a surplus in our country that can be transported overseas, and there is also a need for our country's medicinal materials overseas. Often, due to the payment of taxes, the price is not suitable, resulting in the suspension of transportation. Therefore, the payment of taxes hinders the export of our country's medicinal materials, which is a pity. For this reason, we especially request your esteemed council to forward this memorial to the Ministry of Finance, taking advantage of the fact that the standards for reducing and exempting export taxes are still under negotiation, to request that all export medicinal materials be exempt from taxes, in order to maintain business difficulties and to promote domestic goods. We await orders with trepidation." After investigation, Chinese medicinal materials are exported to places where overseas Chinese gather. For example, in Vietnam, the export of domestic medicinal materials at its peak reached more than 800,000 taels of silver per year. Later, French pharmacists, envious of its benefits, instigated the government to obstruct it in various ways, and the exports have gradually decreased year by year. This matter is related to the needs of overseas Chinese medical treatment and is also a natural product that can cultivate the population. It is urgently necessary to exempt taxes to encourage exports in order to increase by-products, help save rural areas, and plug loopholes. According to the previous situation in the letter, it is reasonable to submit a memorial. We request your ministry to review and approve the inclusion of exported medicinal materials in the tax exemption list, which would be of public benefit.

Page 10

Literacy Promotion Week Closed Yesterday; Surveys to Begin in All Districts Today; Survey Committees Organized Separately to Oversee the Work; Surveys to Begin Today, Completion Scheduled for the End of the Month; Municipal Education Bureau Has Ordered Faculty and Students of All Schools to Assist

According to Shanghai News, the city's literacy education promotion week closed yesterday. To clarify the number of illiterate people in the city in order to allocate the number and location of schools, survey committees have been organized in various districts, and the survey work will begin today. The survey is scheduled to be completed by the end of the month. Details are recorded as follows:

Closed Yesterday

Since the beginning of Literacy Promotion Week on May 1, industry, agriculture, commerce, schools, radio broadcasting, film, entertainment, and other sectors have expanded publicity on a daily basis, which has enabled the citizens of this city to have a considerable understanding of the significance of literacy education and the methods of the municipal government in promoting literacy education. The promotion week closed yesterday, and the association also stipulated continued publicity measures to avoid short-term efforts. The main points are as follows: (1) Surveyors should carry books and leaflets with them when surveying out-of-school people and distribute them at any time. They should also add advice when questioning the people; (2) literacy schools should hold more parent-teacher conferences or recreational activities and should contact local community groups and schools to carry out literacy campaigns; (3) when the Public Security Bureau conducts household registration checks or when newly relocated residents come to the bureau to register, it should inquire at any time whether there are illiterate people and should guide them to nearby literacy schools to contact for enrollment; (4) this association also paints books or texts about literacy education on the walls of main streets; (5) this association contacts film companies to produce one or two films of the literacy movement for screening at any time.

Organize a Committee to Investigate

In order to clarify the situation of out-of-school people in the city so that literacy education can be implemented, a survey committee was specially established in each district to assist the district office in handling the survey of out-of-school people. Since the establishment of district offices on May 1, survey committees have been organized. The committee members are selected from the principals of public and private schools in each district, the directors of public and private social education institutions, the heads of the Public Security Bureau, party committee members, municipal committee members, defense regiment leaders or captains, and those who are enthusiastic about public welfare and enjoy popular support. A survey director is also appointed. The tasks of the survey committee, in addition to surveying out-of-school people aged 13 to 50 living in the district, also include surveying the locations of schools, private schools, social education institutions, temples, guilds, and public places in the district for the purpose of borrowing them to set up literacy schools. Survey personnel are selected from school faculty and staff, upper grades of primary schools, students from secondary schools and below, social education institution staff, Public Security Bureau chiefs, district branch party members, and local leaders.

Depart Today

In addition to the Jiangwan Experimental District, which has completed the survey, and the Confucius Temple Experimental District, which has begun the survey, the other ten districts have all scheduled to begin the survey at the same time today. Survey forms have been distributed to each district. In addition to the items of name, gender, age, and occupation, there are also literacy level (divided into completely illiterate, knowing one-half, four-sixths), free time to go to literacy schools, which month is the most inconvenient, detailed address, and the number of literate and illiterate people in the family must be filled in. Surveyors also carry a 600-word list. When surveying, they first ask each person whether they are literate and ask them to try to read the 600-word list. If they can read one or two lines in a row without difficulty, they are considered literate people. Otherwise, they are considered illiterate people, and they start filling out the survey form. If the surveyor cannot decide, they should ask them to read a few more lines or read the entire list. If they know more than five-sixths, they are considered literate people.

Assistance from All Schools

The Municipal Education Bureau issued an instruction to the municipal primary and secondary schools in this city, which stated, "Case approved by the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee, Literacy No. 47, to the effect that the district offices of this committee will be established on May 1, and the district survey committees will also begin to be organized. All the work of surveying illiterate people in all districts of the city has been decided after research, following the example of your bureau's survey of out-of-school children last year, mobilizing the faculty and staff of municipal primary and secondary schools and upper-grade students, based on the spirit of labor service, to assist in the handling. Now, a copy of the method of surveying out-of-school people by this committee and 1,000 copies of the publicity outline are sent to your bureau. Please inform the principals of municipal primary and secondary schools to instruct all faculty and staff and upper-grade students to provide full assistance in the survey of out-of-school people in this committee's district offices. Please also oil-print the method of surveying out-of-school people by this committee together with the publicity outline and distribute them to facilitate the progress. Sincerely, etc." Attached is the method of surveying out-of-school people and the publicity outline for promoting literacy education. Wu Hua Bank Case: Fan Shaoliang Appeals Against the Original Judgment

After the Shanghai branch of the Guangzhou Wu Hua Industrial Trust Bank at 130 Ningbo Road in the Public Concession and the Wu Hua Branch branch at the intersection of Gao Baolu Road and Xiafei Road in the French Concession closed down in August of last year, the depositors, savings depositors, and ten other creditors of the two banks filed a complaint with the criminal court, stating that the bank had been closed for a long time and there was no indication of the creditors' rights. They appointed a lawyer to accuse Fan Shaoliang, Jian Yu, Ye Haitian, Wu Yousan, Xie Zhizhi, Tang Yushan, Counselor Tang Shoumin, Chen Bingqian, and others, managers and deputy managers of the two branches of the Wu Hua Bank, of fraud and breach of trust, and requested legal action to be taken against them in accordance with the banking regulations issued by the Ministry of Finance. After repeated hearings and investigations by Judge Zhang Chaozu of the Special Court, a verdict was rendered on the 15th of last month. Fan Shaoliang and Ye Haitian (deputy manager of the branch) were each fined 1,000 yuan for operating a savings bank business without the approval of the Ministry of Finance, which could be commuted to one day of imprisonment for every three yuan. They were found not guilty of the charges of fraud and breach of trust, and the remaining defendants were found not guilty. These details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Fan and Ye are dissatisfied with this judgment and have appointed lawyers Jiang Yiping and Hua Maosheng to file an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court with the Second Court, requesting that the case files be sent to the High Court. A hearing will be held soon.

The Fisheries Protection Office Intercepts Fishing Boats; The Haihu Patrol Ship Sinks Pirates

The fisheries patrol ships of the Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry have been sparing no effort in arresting pirates. Recently, they discovered a fishing boat with 15 hostages in the Mazi waters. The details are as follows: The Jin Xiangmao ice-fresh fishing boat was buying fresh fish in the outer sea on the 4th of this month and was fully loaded to return to Shanghai. When passing through the Yangshan waters, a pirate ship with more than 20 pirates suddenly approached the Jin Xiangmao ice-fresh fishing boat, threatened it with guns, and forced the ship to sail to Mazi in an attempt to rob it. Unexpectedly, on the 5th, when it arrived in the Mazi waters, it encountered the Haihu patrol ship of the No. 2 Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry, which was patrolling the waters. The patrol ship found the two ice-fresh fishing boats suspicious and ordered them to stop for investigation. Unexpectedly, the pirates ignored the order and accelerated to escape. The Haihu ship opened fire to stop them. The pirate ship also opened fire in response. After an hour of fierce fighting, the patrol ship's firepower was fierce and hit the mast of the pirate ship. The pirates were finally outnumbered and fled back to the original ship, abandoning the Jin Xiangmao fishing boat. At that time, the sky was already dark, and the wind and waves were strong. The ship still tried to pursue them, but the pirates had already left on the fishing boat and shouted for help. Because the boat needed to protect the equipment of the Yu Zuomao fishing boat, it did not pursue them. In this interception, one Jin Xiangmao ice-fresh fishing boat and 15 crew members were captured. According to the crew, one or two pirates were shot and fell into the water during the fierce battle, and at least five or six people were injured. As the pirates were eager to escape, the ship's life and property were not lost at all.

Cause of Death: Mr. Tie has always valued physical education. In his spare time, he always does various sports. A friend recently brought a horse from Shanxi and Bei.
