Suspected Wife's Infidelity, Committing Suicide with a Sharp Blade, Death So Swift, Case So Strange

Yesterday morning around 9 o'clock, a bloody incident occurred inside an unnumbered tile-roofed house adjacent to the West Zhongxing Cotton Mill on Zhongxing Road, Zhabei. The deceased, named Shen Jifeng, was 35 years old and from Yancheng. He had a wife, Ms. Qi, 26 years old, who was of fair appearance. Shen usually made a living pulling a rickshaw. The day before yesterday, around 5 PM, he went out to pull a night shift, and his wife also went out. According to Ms. Qi, she went to her mother's house in Hongkou. When Shen returned home early yesterday morning around 7 AM, he was extremely angry to find his wife not at home. After 9 AM, Ms. Qi returned from outside, and Shen immediately grabbed and beat her, though not severely. After the beating, Ms. Qi cried at the Lin shop. Shen Jifeng forbade his wife from crying and later threatened her with a sharp blade. Somehow, Shen did not injure his wife, but stabbed himself in the left side of his chest. He immediately bled and fell to the ground. Someone reported the incident to Ning Kaiging, officer number 59 of the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Xinzha branch. The injured man, accompanied by Ms. Qi, was sent to Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road for treatment. However, by the time they arrived at the hospital, he had already lost too much blood. After examination, the doctor determined that he was beyond saving and ordered Shen to be taken home immediately. Upon returning home and entering the door, he breathed his last and died. Officer Ning then took Ms. Qi to the station for questioning and transferred her to the Xinzha branch. He also instructed the local guarantor, Wang Shaoting, to report the incident to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy. Yesterday evening, the deceased was seen lying on a plank door, wearing one each of blue, white, and black cloth short jackets, with a flannel shirt underneath. There was a knife wound on his chest, about a few fractions of an inch wide. He wore black cloth leggings, white cloth shoes, and gray thread socks, and had a Western-style haircut. There were others living with the deceased, but they had all fled. The guarantor sent someone to guard the door. According to neighbors, the deceased had brothers in his hometown, and a 13-year-old daughter named Abao from his previous wife. It is said that someone has already sent a letter to the deceased's hometown to inform them.

Large Quantity of Red Pills Discovered at the South Railway Station, Suspicious Traveler Abandoned Two Suitcases and a Bedroll Unclaimed, 113,211 Red Pills Confiscated

Yesterday morning at 10 AM, the Shanghai South Railway Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, the station police and railway police jointly inspected two suitcases and a bedroll abandoned by a passenger, containing a large quantity of poisonous red pills, totaling 113,211 pills. They were sent to the Songhu Garrison Command for processing. The details are as follows: On the 4th of this month, at approximately 7 AM, a passenger, around 20 years old, carrying two suitcases and a bedroll, arrived at the station and purchased two third-class through tickets from the Shanghai South Station to Yiwu Station, Zhejiang. When the passenger presented the ticket and went to the baggage room to purchase baggage tickets, the baggage clerk, Jiang Xianting, informed the passenger that the suitcases must be inspected according to regulations before they could be weighed and loaded onto the baggage car. The passenger replied that the suitcase keys were with another passenger, and he had forgotten to bring them. He would bring them later to open the suitcases for inspection. After he left, he did not return to claim the suitcases for over three hours. Therefore, the baggage clerk informed the on-duty railway police patrol leader, Xu Ximing, who searched everywhere without success. Subsequently, the baggage clerk, Jiang Xianting, and patrol leader, Xu Ximing, separately reported the matter to their superiors for handling. Han Shangying, the chief of the police section, together with stationmaster Yu Dewen, sealed the abandoned suitcases and bedroll with fire lacquer for safekeeping and temporarily stored them in the police section. In addition to temporarily storing the passenger's two through tickets with the stationmaster, police were dispatched to search everywhere. Like a crane seeking a phoenix, they waited until the morning of the 7th of this month. Because three days had passed without any passenger coming to the station to claim the items, it was deemed suspicious. Therefore, yesterday morning at 10 AM, the police chief Han Shangying, together with the deputy chief of the traffic section Li Guan · and the stationmaster Zhou Binwu jointly opened the suitcases for inspection. The suitcases were found to contain 80 bags of red pills wrapped in cotton quilts, each bag containing approximately 1,000 pills. The other suitcase also contained 39 bags of red pills wrapped in cotton quilts, totaling 119 bags with 113,211 pills. The brand was "Nanyang Company Old Lion Horse Brand." There was also a bedroll, which contained no prohibited items. Because the case involved concealed prohibited poisonous red pills, the police section was not authorized to handle it. In addition to dispatching police to investigate, the 119 bags of red pills, totaling 113,211 pills, two suitcases, and a bedroll were sent to the Songhu Garrison Command for handling at 5 PM yesterday.

Married Woman Sues for Division of Inheritance, Both Parties Should Present Relevant Evidence, Court Orders Out-of-Court Reconciliation, Reschedules Trial

Yao Jingmin, a local woman, 21 years old, whose husband is Mr. Yin, currently the Chinese deputy head of the Public Concession Police Department, residing at No. 32, Lane 455, Jingzhou Road, through her lawyers Jiang Yiping and Li Gengxiang, filed a lawsuit in the Civil Division of the First Special District Court against her elder brother, Yao Shihao, requesting a division of their late father's inheritance. The lawsuit states that their late father, Yin Sheng, had four children: the defendant, Yao Shihao, the plaintiff, Yao Jingmin, Jingmei (female, 16 years old), and Shixiong (male, 14 years old). Yin Sheng passed away on the fourth day of the first lunar month of the 17th year of the Republic of China, leaving behind a residence on Huade Road, nine bungalows on Huishan Road, four acres and five tenths of land, one bungalow on McKinley Road, one acre and three tenths of land on Pingliang Road, two pieces of reclaimed land in Yinxiang Port, a piece of land in Zhenru, and joint ownership of land and savings, worth over 100,000 yuan. All of this is managed by her elder brother, Shihao, who has not divided it according to the law. Therefore, she is filing a lawsuit, requesting a division of one-fourth, totaling 25,000 yuan. Yesterday afternoon, the First Special Court Judge Peng presided over the hearing. Judge Peng first summoned Yao Jingmin to the case and questioned her about the facts of the lawsuit and her economic situation. Because the plaintiff had not paid the litigation fees, although she requested litigation assistance, observing the plaintiff's clothing and assessing her situation, she was not a person unable to pay the fees. Therefore, she was ordered to pay them. Then, Attorney Feng stated that Yao Shihao, 24 years old, from Shanghai, residing at No. 320 Huade Road, could not attend court today due to illness, and refuted the facts, stating that the houses and land listed in the plaintiff's statement did exist. However, the bungalows on Huishan Road were jointly owned with an uncle, and the land on Pingliang Road was his personal property. Therefore, the actual value of the property was only over 26,000 yuan. After deducting the grandmother's alimony, it was only 20,000 yuan. The plaintiff's one-fourth share was only 5,000 yuan. He also filed a counterclaim, requesting the deduction of 2,550 yuan taken by the plaintiff when she got married, and one-fourth of the 6,960 yuan owed for the grandfather's funeral and debts. Furthermore, the reclaimed land was jointly owned by the public and should not be divided. Yao Jingmin admitted that she did receive 2,550 yuan, but claimed that 2,000 yuan was given by her mother, Ms. He, as a loan that she had collected to buy wedding clothes, etc. The court stated that both parties should provide relevant evidence and adjourned the trial, ordering them to reconcile out of court.

West Gate, 50th Anniversary of the Women and Children's Hospital, Hoping for Donations from All Sectors

The Women and Children's Hospital in the West Gate, renowned as the "Red House," was established in 1885. This year marks its 50th anniversary, and a commemorative meeting will be held this Saturday. The hospital is the largest and oldest women's hospital in Shanghai, established initially with a donation of 5,000 yuan from Ms. McGregor Williamson. It started with a basic structure and has grown to its present state through 50 years of hard work and constant reforms. Its contributions to the Chinese people are truly significant. Although the hospital is most famous for its obstetrics department, its internal and external medicine departments are also highly skilled, with specialized physicians in charge of diagnosis and treatment. Since 1885, the number of patients treated by the hospital has exceeded 1.5 million, and over 1,000 babies are born at the hospital each year. Therefore, over the years, 40,000 babies have been born at the hospital. The hospital currently has three sections: one is the Shanghai Women's Medical College and the affiliated Nursing School, with an outpatient department on the ground floor that provides daily diagnosis and medication, which is extremely crowded. The second section is the obstetrics department with the latest equipment, and the third section is the internal and surgical department, which is well-organized, demonstrating the management's meticulous efforts and dedication. The hospital was established entirely for charitable purposes. Most patients only pay 50 cents per day, while the hospital's expenses amount to 2.5 yuan. Therefore, in addition to regular funding and external donations, the hospital must rely on income from private rooms. However, due to the poor market conditions, patients are tightening their expenses. Those who used to stay in private rooms are now staying in second-class rooms, and those who used to stay in second-class rooms are now staying in third-class rooms. As a result, the hospital's income has greatly decreased, and it must rely on external donations for support. Fortunately, there are many charitable individuals in all sectors who can take advantage of the hospital's 50th anniversary to generously donate. A donation of 1,000 yuan can provide two weeks of hospitalization for 15 impoverished patients, a donation of 500 yuan can provide one week of hospitalization for 15 patients, and a donation of 250 yuan can cover the expenses of 10 mothers in the hospital's obstetrics department. If 100 people each donate 100 yuan, it can offset the hospital's annual funding shortfall. Those who donate not only contribute to the development of this charitable cause but also bring blessings to themselves and safety to society. The names of donors of more than one yuan will be engraved on plaques for permanent commemoration.

American Lumber Prices to Increase

The Damei Evening News reports that lumber importers in Shanghai have received letters and telegrams stating that the lumber workers' strike in the northwestern states of America is spreading widely. The American lumber export industry may be greatly affected. If so, the price of lumber in Shanghai may increase from US$2.50 per thousand board feet to US$3.00. It is estimated that the strike involves approximately 1,000 lumber mills in five states, with a total of 75,000 to 100,000 workers. They are demanding increased wages and shorter working hours, but have been unsuccessful. According to local lumber merchants, if the workers win this strike, the price of sawn lumber, which usually sells for US$5.00 per thousand board feet, may increase to US$7.50 or more. Therefore, the price in China will also increase accordingly. Although Canadian lumber can take advantage of this opportunity to promote sales, its price will also increase.

Public Works Department Discusses Telephone Issues, Advocates for a Usage-Based System

At the Public Works Department Board meeting on the 24th of last month, the Public Utilities Committee submitted a report on the discussions regarding telephone issues (committee meetings were held before the taxpayers' annual meeting). The minutes of the meeting were approved and recorded by the Board of Directors. The following is a summary of the contents of the minutes:

The current taxpayers (foreign nationals' annual meeting) passed a resolution requesting the Board of Directors to negotiate with the telephone company to postpone the price increase and to form a special committee to conduct investigations. However, the Public Utilities Committee had already considered the expert investigation and believed that hiring experts would be costly. Based on detailed research, it was known that the company's request was not excessive. Moreover, the company's operational efficiency was not a problem, so it seemed unnecessary. The franchise agreement between the Public Works Department and the company allows the company to earn a profit of one percent of the investment. The Public Works Department made a decision last month that if the French Concession authorities also agreed, the company would be allowed to increase prices from April 1 of this year, with a maximum increase of 12.5%. The Public Utilities Committee then convened a meeting to review the price list, changing the company's original proposed increase of 20.89% to 12.5%, and comparing the impact on users at all levels under the two plans. According to the company's report, commercial and residential telephones in Hong Kong cost 146.25 yuan per year, while in Shanghai, commercial telephones cost 146.85 yuan and residential telephones cost only 90.91 yuan. The former is equivalent, while the latter is 61% more expensive in Hong Kong. The Director of Finance proposed using a usage-based system, proposing to change the residential telephone fee from the originally planned 8 yuan to 8.5 yuan, with the minimum fee for commercial telephones remaining at 10 yuan, but presenting several levels of classification for usage-based calculation. The committee's discussion focused on how to evenly distribute the burden to be commensurate with the company's service. If a usage-based system is adopted, large users will bear more, while small and medium users will benefit more. The company had previously pointed out the economics of the usage-based system, stating that if the current level of communication continues unchanged, an additional capital of 3.5 million yuan is needed to purchase additional equipment. One committee member also said that the telephone fee calculation method should not be simplified by retaining the flat-rate system, but should be charged proportionally, as is the case with other public utilities. The company also stated in a letter that if the usage-based system is implemented and the number of calls is reduced by no less than half, it is willing to allocate all the profits to the telephone fee revision account for a period of one year. According to the General Manager's report, the former telephone company implemented a partial usage-based fee system in 1925. The former company also proposed to revise the telephone price and charge by usage in 1930. Mr. Ansen, an investigative expert hired in 1929, also advocated adopting a usage-based fee system or a tiered pricing system. When the committee met on April 1, it specially invited company representatives Bao De, Chuan Lan, and Fuli Chiman, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Yu Zuoting (accompanied by Xie Fusheng), and Mr. Windsor (bill broker) to attend the meeting. The Director of Finance stated that the usage-based system is now widely used and should be adopted in Shanghai, but the impact should be tested for at least one year before a decision can be made. Then, the company representatives described the advantages of the usage-based system, but temporarily planned to only apply it to commercial telephones. Since the introduction of automatic switchboards, the number of calls has increased sharply, requiring more equipment. If this continues unchanged, the burden on small users will inevitably increase. Currently, the average number of calls per line per day is 18.33. Therefore, the central station, which was originally designed for 10,000 lines, can now only handle 6,000 lines. After the initial implementation of the usage-based system, the company's revenue will decrease. However, in the long run, it is still worthwhile for both the company and small users. One committee member advocated that the flat-rate system should still be used, as it is more convenient; otherwise, users may decrease. The company representatives stated that the usage-based system is more fair. For example, if a certain family's communication needs suddenly decrease, it would be difficult to reduce fees under the flat-rate system. Also, the counters used by the company are extremely accurate and reliable. The partial use in the past year has been very satisfactory. Mr. Windsor stated that based on six years of research, he strongly advocates adopting a usage-based system, but there are still a few inconveniences to be resolved. The reduction in the number of calls may be about a quarter, and will not reach a half; the latter should not be used as a calculation standard. As for those who currently have five lines and make as many as 10,000 calls per month, and those who make more than 100 calls per day in businesses, accounting for one-fifth, this is too cheap. In short, the allocation of telephone fees should be carefully determined. Xie Fusheng, representing the Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, spoke, requesting the Public Works Department to take into account the situation and keep the price increase as low as possible. Shanghai is different from other places, and the usage-based system should be considered carefully and implemented slowly. With the flat-rate system, everyone can predict how much they will pay, and it should not be compared to electricity and gas. The so-called abuse of telephones is an overstatement. When the committee met again, the company stated in a letter that assuming the number of calls will be reduced by 37.5%, a revised fee schedule is as follows: (1) Commercial telephones: 10 yuan per month for up to 150 calls, 3 cents for each additional call, 5 yuan for each additional line; (2) Residential telephones: 8.4 yuan; (3) Private dedicated lines: 2 yuan for every half-mile, 1 yuan for every tenth of a mile, 1 yuan per telephone; (4) Same (5) Socks, 50 cents each; (6) Installation and relocation are 10 yuan each; (7) Branch lines are 1 yuan each; (8) Private switchboards: 5 yuan for one line, 7 yuan for fifteen lines, 10 yuan for twenty-five lines, 12 yuan for thirty-six lines, 14 yuan for forty-seven lines, and 16 yuan for fifty-eight lines; (9) Reconnection fee: 2 yuan. According to the company's written opinion, excluding various unresolved issues, the company's net profit would still be no more than 9.22%. If the number of calls is reduced to 40%, the net profit will be less than 9%, but it seems to still be able to obtain 8%. In this way, only the general reserve fund company will suffer a slight loss of interest. However, the usage-based fee system is fair to users and avoids the hassle of revising the price list in the future. Moreover, this system is uniformly adopted by major cities, so it is willing to help the Public Works Department to realize it. As for the number of commercial machine calls, the company still estimates that it will decrease by 40% to 50%, because Chinese people often handle business outside of office hours and can use their home telephones. According to current predictions, about 40% of businesses will not increase their telephone bills or may even reduce them compared to the old system. Subsequently, the Director of Finance reported that the company's revised calculation basis seemed reasonable. The US income tax and the headquarters' management remuneration were not included, and the depreciation amount was reduced by 150,000 yuan. These issues will be resolved separately. According to experience elsewhere, it seems quite possible that the number of calls will be reduced by 37.5%, and the company can obtain a profit of 9.22% in the year before the end of March next year. The average increase in telephone fees is 11.09%. At that time, the committee decided not to put forward a specific proposal for the telephone case, as the taxpayers' annual meeting would propose a telephone case, and would discuss it later.

Traveler in Ningbo Merchant Hotel Attempts Suicide by Poison

Last night at 9 PM, a traveler, claiming to be Pan Shuangdu, 34 years old, from Xiaoshi, arrived at the Ningbo Merchant Hotel at No. 465 Tianjin Road. The tea boy led him to room 114. At that time, he told the tea boy that a female guest would be coming shortly. The tea boy agreed and left. Who knew that the traveler, due to financial hardship, attempted suicide by taking poison. At noon the next day, someone discovered him and immediately reported it to the tea boy, who called an ambulance to take Pan to Renji Hospital for treatment.

French Police Ban Rumors

Recently, in the evenings, ignorant and idle people have been gathering near the Sino-French School in the Eight Immortals Bridge area, watching the red light on the school's glass windows. Some malicious people have taken the opportunity to spread rumors, claiming that a certain deity has appeared in this red light. The ignorant and foolish people have spread the rumors, believing them to be true. The red light found at the school is entirely due to the reflection of the neon lights of the Golden Theater and is not surprising. To stop the rumors, the French police have banned local tabloids from publishing any strange news about this matter, and will severely punish violators.

Life Bookstore Publishes "World Library"

The Life Bookstore on Fuzhou Road in Shanghai has recently started publishing a "World Library," edited by Guo Zhenduo. Over a hundred famous writers, including Cai Yuanpei and Lu Xun, are specially commissioned contributors. The content includes translations of great masterpieces and new publications of rare and secret books. It encompasses world literary masterpieces from Egypt, Hebrew, India, China, Greece, and Rome to modern Europe, America, and Japan. All first-class works are included. One volume is published each month, twelve volumes per year. Subscription methods: For one-time payment, Category A is 14 yuan per year, 7.5 yuan for half a year; Category B is 9 yuan per year, 4.6 yuan for half a year. For installment payments, Category A requires an initial payment of 5 yuan, followed by monthly payments of 1 yuan for ten months, totaling 15 yuan. Category B requires an initial payment of 3 yuan, followed by monthly payments of 7 dimes for ten months, totaling 10 yuan. Postage is added separately. The first volume is expected to be published in mid-May. The table of contents includes "Biographies of Great Greek and Roman Figures" by Hu Zhongchi, "The Adventures of Don Quixote" by Chuan Donghua, "Dead Souls" by Lu Xun, and "My Memories" by Mao Dun, among ten foreign works. Chinese works include "Collection from Among the Flowers," "Miscellaneous Dramas of Journey to the West," "Jin Ping Mei," and "Jingshi Tongyan," among nine titles. Exquisite samples are printed and will be sent upon request.

Medical News

Dr. Huang Cheng's Enthusiasm for Medicine

Medical Doctor Huang Cheng has profound medical knowledge and rich experience. He has mastered treatment for rheumatic diseases (such as arthritis) and is skilled in internal and external medicine. He studied medicine in Japan for four years and in Germany for twelve years, holding a national examination graduation diploma and having passed the doctoral degree examination. After completing his studies, he successively served as a physician in the internal, external (rheumatism), and venereal disease departments of Berlin University Hospital. In 1930, he returned to China and served as the director of the external (rheumatism) and venereal disease departments of Furen Hospital in Fuzhou. In 1933, he returned to Germany to study new methods of treatment for various departments. This year, he returned to Shanghai, bringing many newly invented special effective injectable medicines and new-style treatment equipment. Currently, he provides free medical services to the poor and sick every Monday to Friday from 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM, waiving consultation fees. The clinic is located along the river north of the Sichuan Road Bridge opposite the General Post Office, telephone 45651. Consultation hours are from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM.

Weather Report

The meteorological forecast from Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The Shandong area is clear and dusty, with strong winds from the southwest to northwest. This is due to a low-pressure system passing through Manchuria and moving northeast-east. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy to clear, with morning fog. Southwest to northwest winds are quite strong. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait are turning cloudy with strong north to east winds. The area between the Ogasawara Islands and the globe has bad weather with cyclones and rain, due to a low-pressure system passing through and moving northeast-east. Yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM was 84.7 degrees, and the lowest was 56.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 89.1 degrees, and the lowest was 61.5 degrees.

Special Report

Bank of Communications Business Report (10)

From the above observations, it can be seen that the Bank's efforts in agricultural investment this year are significant. Regarding rural lending, the former was handled indirectly in conjunction with various banks because the cooperative organization was not yet sound and the Bank's institutions had not penetrated the interior. The amount was not large. This year, branches in the Northwest, Qin, and Shaanxi have been successively established, and the organization of cooperatives has gradually become complete. The opportunity to start direct lending is complete. In addition to the Northwest branches actively lending to cooperatives, it is also planned to jointly establish the China-America Agricultural Loan Syndicate with the Shanghai JinCheng and Zhejiang Industrial Banks and other provincial farmers' banks. A head office will be set up in Shanghai, and offices will be set up in Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, Hebei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other places. The main focus will be on cotton and wheat lending. The fund is tentatively set at five million yuan, shared by each bank according to its share. The syndicate will be established soon, and offices in various regions are also being planned separately. (6) Assisting National Goods Industry

In recent years, the national goods industry has gradually emerged. As a bank for developing industry, the Bank should allocate a portion of funds to provide practical assistance to this emerging industry. This year, larger domestic textile factories, dyeing factories, flour mills, sugar mills, paper mills, and chemical factories that are operating steadily but lack working capital are selected for lending more than in previous years. Regarding investment methods, in addition to striving for strict procedures and solid repayment funds, special attention is paid to the factory's operating income and expenditure.

(7) Promoting Transportation Construction

The Bank has a long history of relationship with the transportation industry. Since its reorganization into a bank for developing industry, it has realized the necessity of promoting transportation construction due to the interrelationship between transportation and industry. This year, it continued to follow this policy and make progress. On the one hand, it provides convenience of deposit, remittance, and exchange to completed projects, and on the other hand, it connects with other banks to jointly invest in uncompleted projects to promote their realization. In total, the amount of joint investment with various banks in transportation construction this year reached 70 million yuan, of which the Bank participated with an investment of more than 7 million yuan. In addition, the Bank's separately extended loans to local transportation authorities were not few.

(8) Promoting Cooperation Among Banks

In recent years, social and economic organizations have become increasingly complex, and the scope of banking business has also expanded. To adapt to the trend and jointly ensure safety, it is necessary to promote cooperation among banks. Significant progress has been made in actively pursuing this over the past year. In Shanghai, joint lending and lending with the Central and China Banks to rescue the market, and cooperation with various banks to handle rural loans. In Jinan, joint investment with the China and Shanghai Banks to jointly operate warehouses, and the establishment of lending conventions to be followed. In Wuhu, jointly leasing land on the riverside of Wuzha Road with the China and Shanghai Banks to set up public warehouses. In Hangzhou, the establishment of a clearing house with various banks and joint financing of silk and silk products. In Nantong, jointly building warehouses with the Bank of China. The uniformity of loan values and interest rates for supervised and secured loans, the public deliberation of railway bill of lading mortgages, and the prudent handling of procedures are all manifestations of the spirit of interbank cooperation.

(9) Improving Personnel Management

In recent years, the Bank has focused on investment in production enterprises, and its business scope has been increasingly expanded. Not only must there be a deep understanding of the situation of various industries, but specialized academic knowledge in factory management and manufacturing technology is also necessary to cope with. Considering that the Bank's branches are located all over the country, it is difficult to equip such talents in all locations. The head office has the responsibility of comprehensively overseeing the Bank's business and guiding and assessing the branches. It is appropriate to recruit talents to facilitate the facilities. Therefore, several commissioners have been transferred and assigned to four groups: cotton industry, salt industry, transportation industry, and economic research, to be responsible for investigation and design matters. At the same time, in view of the increase in the Bank's institutions and the shortage of existing personnel for deployment, various probationary employee regulations have been formulated, using screening methods and examination systems as the criteria for recruiting talents. Examinations have been held twice this year, and graduates have been selected from various universities once. All recruited employees have undergone rigorous training to seek further improvement.

All of the above have been implemented. How effective it is cannot be determined. At this time when world trends continue to evolve and the domestic economy is expected to improve, the continued improvement of the Bank's business depends on future efforts.

Educational News

Dutch East Indies Government Orders Chinese Schools to Prohibit Registration with the Ministry of Education and Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission

(Batavia News) Chinese schools in the Dutch East Indies were originally restricted by the Dutch East Indies government's regulations on private schools. In view of the fact that various Chinese schools have registered with the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the National Government, the Dutch East Indies government recently issued an order to all Chinese schools prohibiting registration with government agencies in our country. The text is as follows: "The majority of private Chinese schools in the Dutch East Indies have been persuaded to register with Chinese government agencies and have registered. Regulations stipulate that those who promote Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Three Principles of the People and Kuomintang believers will be recognized for registration. The basis for registration by the Chinese government is contrary to the principle of 'no politics in schools.' Because the registration regulations require the promotion of the Three Principles of the People and the hiring of teachers who can achieve this goal, I sincerely inform the Dutch East Indies government that it is forced to stop. All Chinese teachers and staff who have been registered with the Chinese government will be expelled from the territory of the Dutch East Indies. Because they are employed in Chinese government-registered Chinese schools, it is obvious that they want to promote the above-mentioned politics prohibited by the Dutch East Indies government in the schools. The above-mentioned items will be implemented in all Chinese schools three months later, or the teachers who will be teaching will be limited to three months. The school board affairs must state their attitude towards registration with the Chinese government. Regarding the statement that the registration with the Chinese government has been abandoned, evidence must be provided, which is the official document from the school board to the Chinese Ministry of Education or the Nanjing Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission." According to this, the education of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies is about to be completely destroyed. It is hoped that the people of the country will protest and strive for it.

After the Promulgation of the Degree Awarding Law, University Graduation Certificates Will Be Revised

The Legislative Yuan passed the twelve articles of the Degree Awarding Law. After it was promulgated by the National Government, the Ministry of Education recently ordered it directly to all colleges and universities and the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities for compliance. Hu Shuhua, president of Hunan University, also telegraphed to inquire whether the word "Bachelor" should be filled in on the certificates of university graduates this summer. The Ministry of Education is currently reviewing and replying. However, it is found that the university graduation certificates that have been submitted by various provinces and cities to the Ministry of Education for inspection and printing in the past have the words "After completing the study period in a certain department and passing the examination, graduation is approved and may be called a certain Bachelor" in the certificate. According to the provisions of Article 3 of the now promulgated Degree Awarding Law, there is a statement that "Anyone who has studied in a public or registered private university or independent college, has completed the study period, has passed the examination, and has been reviewed by the Ministry of Education without objection, will be awarded a Bachelor's degree by the university or independent college." Therefore, the words "may be called" in the graduation certificate of university or independent college graduates in the future will be canceled and simply changed to "is a certain Bachelor." It is heard that the university graduation certificates before that will be revised, and new-style revised university graduation certificates can be implemented this summer.

The Municipal Party Department Actively Promotes Literacy Education

Determined that various groups will establish literacy schools, with all party members responsible for teaching the public

The Literacy Education Promotion Association organized by the Shanghai Municipal Party Department convened its second staff meeting at the Municipal Party Department meeting room at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Standing director Tong Xingbai presided over the meeting, and staff member Gu Shaoyan recorded the meeting. The meeting opened as usual. First, the chairman reported on the recent work situation, and then proposed various implementation methods. It was resolved that: (1) Implementation methods for various groups to establish literacy schools, (2) Methods for all party members to teach the public literacy, (3) Methods for party departments at all levels to promote literacy education, (4) Stipulation of office schedule, etc. All were revised and passed. (5) It was decided to submit the methods for various groups to establish literacy schools passed at the last conversation meeting to the Municipal Executive Committee for approval and record this Thursday. The methods are recorded as follows: (1) All groups approved or registered by the municipal party and government organs have the nature of serving the society and should have the responsibility of supporting public welfare. At this time when the government is developing literacy education, each should do its best to achieve a great cause, which is a generally accepted principle. (2) All groups mentioned in the previous article must, in accordance with their local location, hire teachers and establish at least one literacy school. (3) The number of people in the literacy school established by the previous group must be at least ten people. (4) The previous school must teach for at least two hours per day, and the study period must be at least two months. (5) Before the establishment of the previous school, the school address, the teacher requested, and the teaching time must be reported to the Municipal Party Department for record in accordance with the regulations. (6) When the previous school graduates or finishes its operation, it must be reported to the Municipal Party Department for record. (7) Each literacy school is designated as one term for two months. Each group must run at least one term. Those who want to continue running can do so. (8) The name of each literacy school established by each group must comply with the following regulations and be approved by the Municipal Party Department for record. (9) Groups with special difficulties that have been verified and approved by the Municipal Party Department may be exempted from establishing a literacy school. (10) All literacy schools established by groups must not charge any fees. (11) The school expenses of the schools established by the groups are borne by the groups themselves. Books are issued by the Literacy Education Promotion Association. (12) If it is inconvenient for various groups to establish literacy schools on their own due to location or talent reasons, they may entrust the Literacy Education Promotion Association to handle it on their behalf, but the school name must still be crowned with the name of the group. (13) The expenses for the literacy schools handled on behalf of the group are as follows: The entrusted group pays the association in one lump sum and receives a receipt. Category A: 70 or more students in the morning and afternoon classes, with a teacher's salary and office expenses of 45 yuan per month. Category B: 50 or more students in the morning and afternoon classes, with a teacher's salary and office expenses of 40 yuan per month. Category C: 20 or more students in the morning and afternoon classes, with a teacher's salary and office expenses of 35 yuan per month. (14) Whether the organization of each group is sound and whether the leadership is effective will be evaluated based on the results of this literacy education. (15) If a group is able to organize but delays in implementing it except for the situation in Article 9, the person in charge will be replaced or the group will be disbanded, depending on the severity of the circumstances, as a warning to those who are loosely organized and have ineffective leadership. (16) Groups or persons in charge who have established two or more literacy schools or have held two or more consecutive terms with results will be awarded medals or certificates by the Municipal Party Department. (17) This method is mandatory, and all groups must comply with it. (18) This method will be implemented after being promulgated by the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau. (19) This method may be revised at any time if there are any omissions.

City Education Bureau Order: Educational Research Associations in Each District

Decide on Attending Representatives According to Procedures and Report Research Results Promptly. The Shanghai City Education Bureau issued an order to the chairmen of primary education research associations in each district, stating: It has been found that the primary education research associations in each district have been established at different times, and many have failed to complete the research topics issued by the Ministry of Education within the prescribed time. Furthermore, the representatives from each district to the citywide primary education research association have often not been determined according to the prescribed procedures. The Ministry's ten research topics must be reported by the end of May, and the date for the citywide primary education research association's general meeting has been set for early May. All representatives from each district attending the general meeting and the results of all research topics must be submitted to the bureau within three days of receiving this document, so that they can be printed and submitted for discussion at the general meeting. It is hereby ordered that the chairmen of each district comply and not delay further. This is a firm order.

Joint Annual Meeting of Five Academic Organizations: First Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

Determining the Name of the Joint Annual Meeting and Electing Yang Xiaoshu and Others as Executive Members

Five academic organizations, including the Science Society of China, were invited by Guangxi Province this year and decided to hold a joint annual meeting in Nanning. Yesterday, representatives from each academic organization held the first preparatory meeting at the Science Society of China to discuss all matters related to the event. Details are as follows:

Attending Representatives: Including representatives from the Chinese Institute of Engineers: Jun, Zou Enbing; the Botanical Society of China: Qian Chongshu; the Zoological Society of China: Liu Xian; Yu Dao from the Science Society of China: Yang Xiaoshu, Fang Ziwei; and the Geographical Society of China: He Bingsong, totaling eight people. Yang Xiaoshu was elected as chairman, and Zou Enbing as secretary.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Yang Xiaoshu first gave a report, stating briefly that the academic organizations had decided to hold a joint annual meeting in Nanning, Guangxi, this year. Today, representatives from four academic societies and the Science Society of China and the Physics Society of China are present. The Physics Society of China has already scheduled a meeting in Qingdao this year and hopes to participate next year. The Chemical Society of China has not yet decided whether to participate, so currently, only five organizations can jointly hold the annual meeting. The work of this preparatory committee is crucial before the opening of the annual meeting. Several common preparatory matters can be raised for discussion today.

Discussion of Proposals: Next, the following matters were discussed: (1) The issue of the name of the joint annual meeting. It was decided to name it the "Joint Annual Meeting of Five Academic Organizations." The order of the names of the five organizations is arranged according to the number of strokes in the third character, as follows: Chinese Institute of Engineers, Chinese Geographical Society, Science Society of China, Chinese Zoological Society, and Chinese Botanical Society. (2) The issue of the date of the joint annual meeting. It was decided to hold it in early August. The exact date will be determined after investigating shipping schedules at the next meeting.

Annual Meeting Program: (3) The issue of the program for the joint annual meeting. It was decided to set the following principles: A. Matters jointly prepared include the opening ceremony, annual meeting banquet, public lectures, and visits and tours. Matters prepared separately by each organization include proposals and association affairs. Matters jointly prepared by each society and the engineering, zoology, and botany sections of the Science Society of China include the presentation of papers. B. The opening ceremony will be held jointly once. Proposals and association affairs will be held separately four times. For the convenience of members, the Science Society of China will hold two sessions separately, while the other four organizations will each hold one session at the same time. Specialized paper presentations will be held twice, concurrently and separately according to the nature of the papers. General paper presentations will be held jointly once. C. The meeting will last four days, with two sessions each day. Visits and tours will be held jointly for two days. All luncheon banquets will be declined, except for one joint annual meeting banquet for the five organizations.

Funding Issues: (4) The issue of funding for the joint annual meeting. It was decided that A. Each member participating in the joint annual meeting will pay an annual meeting fee of five yuan, regardless of whether they are members of multiple associations and paying fees repeatedly. B. The total income and expenditure of the joint annual meeting will be calculated together. If the expenditure is insufficient, it will be divided into seven shares, with the five organizations sharing the costs. The Chinese Institute of Engineers and the Science Society of China will each bear two shares, and the remaining organizations will each bear one share. C. Participating members may bring only one family member. Other guests will be limited to those invited by the annual meeting. (5) The issue of the five organizations recommending staff for the joint annual meeting. It was decided that each of the five organizations should recommend one member for the annual meeting presidium, one member for the lecture committee to host public lectures, and one member for the program committee to draft the detailed program for the entire meeting.

Election of Standing Committee: (6) The issue of the standing committee of this preparatory committee. It was decided to elect Yang Xiaoshu, Zou Enbing, Liu Xian, and Fang Ziwei as standing committee members, with Yang Xiaoshu as chairman, Zou Enbing as recording secretary, Liu Xian as corresponding secretary, and Fang Ziwei in charge of transportation matters. The Science Society of China will be the location for the standing committee's office. (7) The five organizations jointly recommended Mr. Ma Junwu and Mr. Ma Minghai as members of the joint annual meeting preparatory committee, and the chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government as the honorary chairman of the annual meeting. (8) Other matters to be handled will be discussed at the next meeting. The date of the meeting will be determined by the chairman. The meeting adjourned.

Special Article

The Trend of the Chinese Cultural Movement

(A Lecture by Yi Yuan)

The Chinese cultural movement, which has been interrupted for many years, has recently shown signs of revival due to the stimulation of national humiliation. In the past year, the waves of the cultural movement will move throughout the country, and on the increasingly depressed national psychology, it will also create a new response. If we can advocate properly, avoid repeating the same mistakes, be purely sincere, and not value superficiality, it may indeed be a major turning point in our nation's revival movement. I am ashamed of my insignificance, and last year I accepted an invitation to lecture at the Cultural Society. Due to the urgency of personal matters, I have not yet organized the lecture notes to seek correction from the wise and learned. Time flies, and suddenly it is the May Fourth period. At this time, my feelings are doubled, so I will restate the general idea in the hope of encouraging my fellow citizens.

For the past ten years, I have been working hard and diligently, living a simple and self-disciplined life. All my writings, directly and indirectly, have been aimed at promoting the development of the Chinese cultural movement. I dare not be different in my humble opinion, because culture is the expression of a nation's vitality and competitive power. From a holistic perspective, it is the total material and spiritual achievement of a nation in responding to and improving its environment and striving hard. In terms of its "use," it is an essential element for any nation seeking survival, development, and prosperity. Looking back at history and observing current events, the rise and fall, survival and death of all nations, the judgment of strength and weakness, superiority and inferiority, are all due to the prosperity or decline of their national culture. The reason why China's past history was brilliant and prosperous was due to the development of its culture. The reason why it is now declining and suffering misfortune is due to the decline of its culture. Although the Chinese nation has been conquered by foreign races in history, it has never been eradicated because of the victory of its culture. The reason why it has suffered humiliation from the great powers in the past century is due to the failure of cultural struggle. In the modern world, there is a phenomenon of those who follow the trend surviving and those who resist it perishing. This is the development of scientific culture. Japan initially did not understand this principle, so it was also oppressed by the great powers. After the Meiji Restoration, it quickly caught up and even surpassed them. Therefore, its politics, economy, military, and education were all able to generate powerful forces to compete with the European and American powers. Unfortunately, our people do not understand the principles of modern national survival, and they have completely lost their ability to create culture. They do not strive for self-improvement and rely on others in everything. They have no ability to create or improve any methods or necessities for national survival. This is the root cause of national decline and the summoning of national disaster. We must deeply understand this historical iron rule of national prosperity and decline and strive to develop national culture to strengthen and enrich national vitality.

However, what is the real effect of the cultural movement, which has been sensational for a while? This kind of doubt must be distinguished. The reason why the past cultural movement failed has its own undeniable mistakes. It is not possible to deny the true value of culture because of its mistakes. The reasons for the failure of the past cultural movement in our country can be divided into three points:

First, it was destructive - those who promoted the past cultural movement described their culture as new, but they did not know that the new is invisibly conceived in the old, and it is by no means a sudden emergence outside the old. Therefore, driven by emotional impulses, they blindly hated the "old," and everything old was to be destroyed. They blindly pursued the new, but the new ultimately broke away from the old and ran wild. As for what is new, the masses have no clear impression, how can they be new? The masses have no concrete way to create it, and the resulting abuses are that the advantages of our country's inherent culture have disappeared, and the so-called new culture is still nowhere to be found. This has caused great chaos in the spiritual world, and a gloomy and melancholy atmosphere fills the world. The impetuous are reckless and disregard right and wrong, and the cautious lose their principles. Alas, this is why the moral principles have been lost, and the hearts of the people are prone to chaos.

Second, it was blindly following - the past cultural movement was driven by emotions and blindly pursued the new. Therefore, those who peddled and imported into China, such as liberalism and communism, all failed to meet the needs of our nation. The pathological state of society, economy, and politics in recent years may be said to be the result of this kind of blindly following and anti-national cultural movement.

Third, it was superficial - Yang Xingfo once commented on the New Culture Movement, saying, "The New Culture itself has never been realized, and the New Culture Movement is even more of a fleeting dream that has long disappeared. Those who promote the New Culture Movement are all 'temporary performers who gather from all directions,' 'playing roles in a market,' and 'each showing their own talents.' After the gongs and drums are scattered, it is still a numb and indifferent society." Therefore, the result of the past cultural movement, although it was noisy on the surface for a while, did not actually promote society and enable the general public to benefit from it. In other words, there is still a huge distance between the ideals of the New Culture Movement and the national masses. To be more precise, the knowledge and skills of the national masses have not been improved or increased due to the cultural movement. This is what should be taken as a strong reflection and painful correction.

Learning from the past is the teacher of the future. Those who engage in the cultural movement today should first remember the lessons of the failure of the past cultural movement and accurately grasp the direction that the cultural movement should take today. Now, let us discuss it in detail:

First, it should be constructive - since the essence of culture is the expression of a nation's vitality and competitive power, the purpose of the cultural movement is not negative destruction, but lies in positive construction. Only engaging in destruction harms the nation's vitality, and only striving for construction can cultivate the nation's strength. This so-called construction has two aspects of meaning. Grasping reality and creating new systems are indeed things that construction should have. However, the review and preservation of the advantages of our country's inherent culture should also not be overlooked by those who are truly concerned about the cultural construction of our country.

Second, it should be self-aware - culture is to a nation what food is to the human body and medicine is to a patient. If you swallow it greedily and throw medicine indiscriminately, it will not only be useless to the body, but also enough to lose your life. The cultural movement of the Chinese past has committed this mistake. The nation's life is in danger, and careful recuperation is still uncertain. If you are not careful again, what could be more dangerous? Therefore, those who are engaged in the cultural movement today should be most alert to the fact that they must not repeat the same mistakes and repeat the mistakes of the past. Any foreign cultural relics, systems, doctrines, and theories only have their true value if they are in line with our national spirit, historical background, and social needs. It is also permissible to exert its function after it has been digested by our nation. This is also what those who engage in the cultural movement from now on should pay attention to and be aware of.

Third, it should be pragmatic - the past cultural movement failed to bridge the gap between the level of the masses and the social system. Therefore, the knowledge and skills of the general public have not yet reached the general level. This is why our country's cultural movement is nominally existing and has failed to promote group transportation. Those who engage in the cultural movement today should first try to eliminate the abuses of emptiness and shallowness, be down-to-earth, and go deep among the people to improve the actual lives of the national masses in terms of clothing, food, housing, and transportation, and increase their living ability. As for the political, economic, and social systems of a country, they should be properly and actively created. Extending this to the skills and tools of production of the people throughout the country, even the slightest improvement of a needle and a hoe for workers and farmers should be sought. It is necessary to ensure that all the people in the country, regardless of scholars, farmers, workers, businessmen, men, women, old, and young, can be deeply influenced by the waves of the cultural movement and benefit from it. This is also an essential point to pay close attention to.

In short, today's Chinese cultural movement should strive to avoid the past destruction, blindly follow, and repeat the superficial mistakes, and establish a new direction for it. It should move forward along the path of construction, self-awareness, and pragmatism in order to meet the needs of the nation, cultivate the nation's vitality, improve the intelligence of the national masses, and truly enhance the nation's strength to survive.

Moreover, all movements, the body of which is not our purpose, but only a method of promoting a certain purpose. Therefore, meetings, lectures, newspaper reports, and official announcements are only means of movement, not the purpose of movement. If the organizers of the movement only take meetings, lectures, newspaper reports, and propaganda as their ability, steal false fame, and forget the inherent purpose and true mission of their movement, or even neglect their daily duties, do not engage in their proper business, socialize, compete, and deceive the world with big words, then the nature of their actions is actually unbearable to hear. Then, all movements will only drive the masses to go down the wrong path of vanity, pride, and inferiority, and our great and pure nation will only become increasingly degenerate. Revival? Revival?

The fate of the country is in danger, and destruction is imminent. Worried about the times, I cannot help but say it in a heavy and detailed way. May the virtuous and heroic people of the world take my words and act on them, and I will be happy to be their humble follower.

East Asia and Fudan Track and Field Competition Results

Jia Lianren's 1500 meters in four minutes and twenty-two seconds, only four-tenths of a second off the national record.

For the sake of mutual learning and friendship, the track and field teams of the East Asia Physical Education College and Fudan University held a friendly competition at the Zhizhi College sports field on Shuidian Road at half past one yesterday afternoon. Jiang Xiangqing, Shen Kunnan, Dong Chengkang, Qu Yue, Chu Bomian, Wu Shijie, Zhou Jun, Hu Xidi, and others served as referees. Jia Lianren, a famous middle-distance runner from East Asia, focused all his energy on the 1,500 meters yesterday and completed the entire course in an excellent time of four minutes and twenty-two seconds, less than half a second off the national record (four minutes and twenty-one seconds and four-tenths). If someone were to compete with him, this old record would have long been broken. After a 45-minute break, he competed in the 800-meter race. Jia's physical strength was slightly diminished, and there were few competitors, so he only completed the race in two minutes and ten and a half seconds in a very natural manner. This person is of moderate build, full of vitality, and his future prospects are just beginning. He will surely display his great ambitions in the Double Tenth National Games. Zhou Shunsheng of East Asia's shot put of 12.06 meters, Li Zipu's javelin of 45.15 meters, and Jiang Huairen's triple jump of 12.90 meters were all quite good. Fudan's Qiu Guangxie's high jump has ample elasticity, but unfortunately, he only practiced twice this season, resulting in awkward movements, failing to attract attention from all parties. If he could put in a little more effort, he would definitely be able to dominate the country and not let Wu Bixian have all the glory. If you don't believe it, please wait and see what happens next. (According to general observations, with one month of practice, he should be able to achieve a score of 1.90 meters or more.) In terms of short distances, East Asia no longer has Su Xiaoru, who has already graduated, and Fudan also has no outstanding talents, so the results are particularly poor. However, overall, this competition was quite satisfactory. Fudan is preparing to go to Beijing tomorrow to participate in the Jiangda Sports Association Games. The complete results are listed below:

Beiping, 7th telegram. After the first trial verdict in the case of Liu Jinggui shooting and killing Teng Shuang, the prosecutor originally planned to abandon the appeal. Liangjiang Narrowly Defeated by Boys in Singapore

(Hua News Agency, Singapore) The Liangjiang Women's Southern Expedition Team previously competed in Manila, Java, Surabaya, and other places, going smoothly and invincible, causing the overseas Chinese in the South Seas to praise them endlessly. They arrived in Singapore yesterday and first fought against the Daonan Boys Team, the runner-up in last year's Singapore Chinese basketball tournament. After not much fighting, the main player was injured, resulting in a narrow defeat. The score was 41 to 36.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Qian Yun)

Love and Luck

An insightful woman does not fall in love easily; an insightful woman, once in love, refuses to let go. Such a woman is certainly "lucky"; but "misfortune" often follows her closely.

A Wife Who Loves Firewood and Rice A woman who wants a divorce without firewood and rice will probably fall asleep as soon as she gets into bed. When her husband has plenty of firewood and rice, he will definitely put on airs, and this wife will definitely show a smiling face and be happy to accept it.

First Kiss

Pay attention to your first kiss, savor your first kiss, commemorate your first kiss. The first kiss is the most important, most prosperous, and most glorious page in your life history.

Men's Hearts Are Not Entirely Hard

Women often feel that men's hearts are terribly hard, but when they have their own will, what is so terrible about men's hearts being hard? Besides, men are certainly not all bad-hearted. Women can get real help from men who are not bad-hearted.

Separation

— Jiao Xin

"Living separation" has always been as sad as "death separation." But death cannot be reversed, while separation can be reunited. The most heartbreaking thing is when you are healthy when you leave, but when you come back, you are already in a coffin.

Don't resent the sadness of separation, you must know that without the sad separation, where would the sweet reunion come from!

In childhood, one is reluctant to leave one's parents, in youth, one is unwilling to leave one's lover, and in old age, one sheds tears for the separation of one's children.

When separating, one resents the train or ship for not stopping for a moment longer; when returning, one resents the train or ship for not leaving faster.

The scene of waving hats and scarves in farewell at the station and wharf is the most desolate, so I often say that people who work at the station and wharf are emotionally numb if they are unmoved by this scene.

One who hangs one's head alone, dejectedly, and walks away from the station alone is definitely the one who has just said goodbye.

Liu Bei's felling of trees to send Xu Shu off was certainly because of his deep affection, but I say that half of it was still the tactics he used.

Wu Shang suffered misfortune together with his father because he was thinking of meeting his father. If he had listened to his younger brother at that time, he would not have died, and his father would not have lost his life. Although separation and reunion are small matters, emotions must be restrained by reason.

Funny Stories About Pickpockets

— Wang Shouqiu

Speaking of pickpockets, it can be said that they are famous all over the world. No matter who they are, they have a considerable understanding of them, or many readers may have been pickpocketed by them! Especially at ship docks, train stations, and lively theaters and amusement parks, these places are where these people gather. Therefore, traveling passengers and spectators at lively venues are always at risk of being pickpocketed.

It is said that pickpockets also undergo training. The things they pickpocket must wait three days before they can be exchanged, because they are afraid that the loser is a "big shot." Then the things pickpocketed still have to be returned to him. Was it Wang Hu? When he was the governor of Jiangsu Province, he was once patronized by pickpockets. Or it was when he had just arrived in Nanjing and had not yet taken office, because his clothes were very simple, so the pickpockets actually mistook him for an "old man" and pickpocketed his leather suitcase. So, this Governor Wang was furious, immediately summoned the police chief to scold him, and set a deadline to recover the original items. Within a few hours, the stolen goods and the thief were caught. Not knowing Mount Tai with their eyes, no wonder they touched bad luck!

Everyone knows that pickpocketing is a secret activity, but Soviet Russia has a kind of public pickpocket, this kind of pickpocket sometimes acts as an international pickpocket, and the local government uses them to investigate passengers. Although this does not check passengers on the surface, it is actually more severe than checking. Of course, this kind of pickpocket - actually a thief - has a monthly salary and is protected by the government, which can really make our country's pickpockets envious!

Unimpeded Source!

Water Prison is Better Than Hell

— Qi Zhong

In this publication, there was previously an article by Mr. Defu, "Water Prison," saying that those who work as back scrubbers in bathhouses are immersed in water vapor all day long, and their suffering is more bitter than the "blacksmith, boatman, and tofu grinder," which are generally regarded as the most bitter occupations. Therefore, they - the back scrubbers - are said to be in a water prison. Yes, back scrubbing is indeed more bitter than the occupations of blacksmithing, boating, and tofu grinding. Because blacksmiths seem to suffer the punishment of burning in summer, but in winter, because there is fire to drive away the cold, they can finally live a few happy days; boatmen, although they drink the northwest wind in the cold winter, they also live a few days of poetic life on summer nights with a bright moon and clear wind; as for tofu grinding, now because of the development of science, many have used electricity and do not need to work late at night; even if they work late at night, they also have to sleep during the day, which is certainly better than back scrubbing friends immersed in water vapor. But I think that people in the water prison, although suffering, are not as bitter as those in hell. The so-called people in hell are those who work in hell, that is, miners. Miners walk into the pit to mine, and the pit is unusually dark, which can be regarded as entering the hell where they cannot see the sun. Moreover, the air in the pit is unusually turbid and very humid, so the miners' bodies are not only weakened because they cannot get clean air, but also mostly suffer from damp diseases. They walk into the pit to work, and often have to spend half a month before they can come to the ground to see the sun, which is tens of thousands of times different from the back scrubbers who can walk outside the bathhouse door every day! Back scrubbers can smoke a cigarette when they are tired, but miners cannot at all. Unfortunately, if the ground collapses, the miners will be buried alive in hell, and there is no way to escape. Therefore, when the mining workers enter the pit to work, they also have the heart to sacrifice their lives. If they work for half a month and then return to the ground, it is like being reborn, so they must indulge in prostitution and drinking to be happy. Because their suffering is tens or hundreds of times more bitter than that in the water prison, and their workplace is underground, it is certainly no one will object to calling the mine a hell!

Local Customs Notes

Japanese Wooden Clogs

— Ji Yun

Living in Japan, no matter where you are, you can always hear the clacking sound of wooden clogs. Especially when a Japanese woman wearing wooden clogs walks on the cement sidewalk, the sound is clear and crisp, arousing a strange emotion. In ancient times, people in our country also wore wooden clogs when climbing mountains and enjoying the snow. Now, in the countryside of the mainland, or perhaps some people still wear self-made wooden clogs on rainy days. Japanese wooden clogs, generally called "Geta," come in many varieties. No country in the world has boots that are the same as Japan's. So, it is not impossible to say that "Geta" is a representative of Japan.

"Geta" are divided into two types: those with teeth and those with flat bottoms. Both have two straps on top, which fasten the toes. The place where the two straps cross is where they are embedded in the gap between the big toe and the second toe. When it gets cold, they wear a special kind of short socks called "Tabi," which are sewn from a single or double layer of cloth. They are very much like a sock, with the big toe and the other toes separated, so they can clamp the straps of the "Geta." Men's socks are all black, and women mostly wear white or other colors, but there are no patterns.

Farmers wear "straw sandals" when cultivating in the fields. The style is similar to what rickshaw pullers in our country wear, and there are also ropes to fasten the heels. Ordinary "Zori" are different again. They are not made of straw, but are woven from very thin grass whips. The value is slightly more expensive, with wealthy products costing tens of dollars a pair. Like Zori, there are also two types made of wood and cork. The wooden ones have lacquer and beautiful patterns on top and are especially for women.

There are many kinds of "Geta" worn on sunny days, with names such as "Koma Geta" and "Hiyori Geta." These clogs have very short teeth and are made of a whole piece of wood, sometimes with a piece of leather added to prevent mud. The ones worn by women mostly have leather of various colors to protect the feet, usually red and green. Modern women also wear wooden clogs, which look very much like the sole of a high-heeled leather shoe. There is also a kind of wooden clog with a missing part at the bottom, which makes a shell-shell-shell sound when walking, mostly worn by underage girls. Ordinary wooden clogs cost more than half a yuan and can be used for more than a year.

Wooden clogs without lacquer are no different for men and women. The five-color straps are mostly used by men and women over middle age. Wooden clogs are all made of paulownia wood, which is soft and light. Rubber is often nailed on the teeth to reduce noise, which shows that the Japanese themselves also feel that the sound of walking is too loud. Japanese homes are all covered with mats, which are unusually clean. Whenever you return home, you have to take off your "Geta" and walk into the room with socks on. In larger homes, you also have to change into slippers, walk through the passage, and then take off your slippers and enter the room with socks on. In the past, Japan did not have slippers, so they were called "Slippers." Chinese people do not have the habit of changing shoes, so they all complain endlessly when they first arrive in Japan.

Nowadays, many Japanese wear leather shoes and suits, and many modern women wear high-heeled shoes. For the sake of easy putting on and taking off, they buy very large sizes, and the shoelaces are also fastened very loosely. In addition, having been accustomed to dragging wooden clogs, even if they wear leather shoes, they still drag them, which is extremely funny. Japanese galoshes are often sold in our country's markets, but the Japanese do not wear them. There is another kind of long galoshes there, which are like army boots, costing more than two yuan, but very few people wear them. There is a kind of rubber-soled black cloth quick boots, which are worn by workers and rickshaw pullers.

Small Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode 12 Ashamed of having no clothes, avoiding each other behind curtains, diligently saving lamp oil, copying books at dawn

I now have a small ambition, planning to invite some comrades to edit textbooks with local characteristics, as well as books for adult education. Think about it, letting people in their twenties receive children's education, and letting an editor from Jiangnan tell people on the Northwest Plateau about the social conditions of Jiangnan in books, how can that be appropriate? Zhou Yourong raised his head back to the roof, sighed a long breath, and then said to Zhizhiqian: Mr. Cheng, you are a person with a heart. But what's the use? For example, I, although not a virtuous official, am at least not a corrupt official, but I was driven away by the Eighth Master. All the plans I had for being a county magistrate were useless, I just raised military pay with people for more than half a year. After speaking, he sighed again. Zhizhiqian said: Now the military men in various provinces are somewhat enlightened, and politics may be on the right track one day soon... Zhou Yourong reached out and wiped his face vigorously, indicating that he would cancel what he had just said, and smiled: Don't mention me, let's talk about yours. After talking for a long time, you are all talking about the student's side, what about the teacher's side? Zhizhiqian thought for a moment and smiled slightly: We are all guests in Shaanxi, and there are still some things that we cannot understand clearly. About this, please let our old brother report it. He has relatives who teach in the interior, and he can report some materials. Saying that, he looked at Wang Beihai. Before he spoke, he sighed, as if what he was about to say was another sad article. (199)

Misty Records of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Deling of Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

One morning, when we were all ready to go to the early court with the Empress Dowager, suddenly a eunuch rushed in in a panic, with a kind of terribly solemn look on his face, as if he was afraid of missing something important: he hurriedly brought a report.

"Old Buddha!" He shouted on the ground, excited like a monkey, "This servant just saw that Hei Baoyu has given birth to four puppies, so I rushed to report it."

As soon as the Empress Dowager heard this, a light of joy immediately flashed in her eyes. The "Hei Baoyu" mentioned here is the name of a dog: dogs are something the Empress Dowager loves, or at least it can be said that it is one of the many things that the Empress Dowager loves. Since she loves dogs, she naturally wants to raise dogs, but her raising dogs is very different from ordinary people; she regards this matter as very important and does not neglect it at all. She specially asked people to collect many books that discuss how to choose dog breeds, how to allocate feed, and how to train puppies, and other specialized technical books, for her to read and study in her spare time, so it can be said that none of her dogs are not of clear pedigree and long-standing reputation.

The Empress Dowager also asked me if I had any interest in the animal dog? I told her that I also liked dogs like her; this is the truth, I still like dogs very much! And those dogs I saw at the Empress Dowager's place that day, especially felt precious and cute, most of them are real Beijing small breed dogs, their heads and noses are very short, but their fur is not uniform, there are various colors. (309)

Finance Spring Racing Season Mid-Term, Bullish Trend in Bullion Bidding

Public Sentiment Stimulated by Spot Market, Results in Further Increase of 6.6 Yuan

The gold market has recently been flourishing due to public sentiment being stimulated by the spot market. Yesterday, it continued to rise. However, because the foreign exchange market was inconsistent, it was strong at first but then weakened. Due to the Spring Racing season, trading was only conducted for half a day as usual, so the market situation was quite calm. In the early morning, during the mid-term of the closing period, overseas calls indicated that both the British and American silver markets and forward silver prices had risen slightly, but the amount was very small, and public sentiment was not affected. The pre-market trading closed and immediately rose to 87.8 yuan. Due to a lack of supply, it broke through the 90 yuan mark. Although there was a reversal after entering, the Central Bank's listing was announced. The pound was flat and the US dollar rose, and the customs gold unit increased by one li. The standard price of bullion bidding rose to 828.7 yuan. Public sentiment reversed to become bullish, causing a further rise. The morning opened with high prices and remained stable after opening. However, the foreign exchange market was inconsistent, and banks rushed to sell. HSBC's listing also remained unchanged, gradually retreating within the 90 yuan mark. Major players aggressively bought at lower prices, and HSBC also quickly placed orders, causing a temporary rebound. However, banks continued to sell, and sellers actively traded at higher prices. The Guangdong banking group sold bars in unison, temporarily halting the upward trend, and then retreated within the 90 yuan mark. However, due to major players still coming in to replenish their positions, banks slightly bought at cheap prices, which helped maintain the price. The announcement of the market closure had already been made public, and the market lacked special supply and demand, so the market situation turned calm, with narrow fluctuations. The market situation was mostly sideways, and public sentiment had not turned bearish. The underlying trend was still promising, leading to a stable closing. The half-day market situation was stable. Various syndicates are taking a wait-and-see attitude, wanting to take action only after the market moves. The market became sluggish. Shorts thought the market was too stagnant, and taking a loss on the swap, so they were unwilling to take bold actions.
